22. Why this spec is the right starting point
This is the correct first deep spec because Topic Intelligence is already:

the deepest local reasoning engine,

the richest producer of downstream signals,

the engine Coverage uses for proof and false-mastery overrides,

the engine Timing uses indirectly through delayed recall and intervention follow-up,

the engine Risk uses through intervention failure and topic-state consequences,

and the engine Adaptation uses through family effectiveness history.

The best next move is Spec Pack 2B — Topic Intelligence algorithm sheet, where I define:

precise formulas,

threshold constants,

confidence math,

reroute thresholds,

proof checkpoint rules,

and blueprint composition rules in executable detail.


proceed

I’m tightening this from build structure into the actual algorithm sheet now: thresholds, scoring math, reroute rules, proof gates, and blueprint composition logic. This is the layer that makes the engine implementable instead of descriptive.

Thought for 10s
Below is Spec Pack 2B — Topic Intelligence Algorithm Sheet.

I’m keeping a hard line between:

Audited current behavior — already present in your engine audit.

Proposed default constants/rules — the next layer I recommend formalizing for implementation.

Your current audited Topic engine already has the core algorithmic spine we are extending: an 18-step pipeline, 8-dimensional concept ranking, 7 hypothesis families, 9 teaching modes with evidence override and intervention reroute, a 6-checkpoint proof contract, a 17-metric evidence spine, evidence ingestion, and feedback-loop closure. 

 


1. Algorithm sheet purpose
This document answers:

what exact scores are computed,

how hypotheses are seeded and updated,

what thresholds trigger reroutes,

how proof is computed,

how entry points are chosen,

how a session blueprint is assembled,

when delayed recall is scheduled,

and what minimum evidence is required before the engine acts decisively.

The goal is to make Topic Intelligence executable and testable, not just conceptually rich.

2. Canonical score ranges
Every Topic Intelligence score should normalize to 0.0 .. 1.0.

Use this convention:

0.00 - 0.24 = very weak

0.25 - 0.39 = weak

0.40 - 0.59 = unstable

0.60 - 0.74 = usable

0.75 - 0.89 = strong

0.90 - 1.00 = very strong

These are proposed defaults for consistency across:

concept ranking inputs,

evidence rates,

hypothesis confidence,

proof checkpoints,

flags like fragility, transfer, recall, speed, confidence.

3. Evidence sufficiency gate
Before Topic Intelligence is allowed to emit a strong dominant diagnosis, it should test evidence sufficiency.

3.1 Audited base
The current engine already builds an evidence spine from up to 250 normalized topic evidence points plus up to 400 response rows. 


3.2 Proposed sufficiency formula
evidence_sufficiency =
  0.30 * volume_score +
  0.20 * recency_score +
  0.20 * modality_score +
  0.15 * consistency_score +
  0.15 * representation_score
Component definitions
volume_score

0.00 if < 6 usable evidence points

0.35 if 6..11

0.60 if 12..19

0.80 if 20..34

1.00 if >= 35

recency_score

based on share of evidence from last 14 days

recent_points / total_points, capped to 1.0

modality_score

measures whether evidence spans enough useful conditions:

untimed

timed

transfer

mixed_context

retrieval

delayed_recall

covered_modalities / 6.0

consistency_score

if evidence wildly conflicts, confidence should drop

1.0 - stddev(bucket_scores) clamped to 0..1

representation_score

representation variety from the audited evidence spine is already tracked. 


use normalized coverage across:

verbal

symbolic

visual

applied

mixed

3.3 Gate policy
if evidence_sufficiency < 0.35:

no dominant hypothesis

status = Defer

entry point = DiagnoseFirst

if 0.35 <= evidence_sufficiency < 0.55:

dominant hypothesis allowed only if margin over runner-up is >= 0.18

if evidence_sufficiency >= 0.55:

normal diagnosis permitted

4. 8-dimensional concept ranking
4.1 Audited current formula
The current engine ranks concepts using 8 weighted dimensions:

dependency importance 0.20

exam leverage 0.18

misconception risk 0.15

difficulty 0.12

transfer importance 0.10

speed sensitivity 0.10

confidence sensitivity 0.10

abstraction level 0.06

minus compaction penalty up to 0.12 


4.2 Canonical formula
concept_rank =
    0.20 * dependency_importance
  + 0.18 * exam_leverage
  + 0.15 * misconception_risk
  + 0.12 * difficulty
  + 0.10 * transfer_importance
  + 0.10 * speed_sensitivity
  + 0.10 * confidence_sensitivity
  + 0.06 * abstraction_level
  - compaction_penalty
4.3 Proposed compaction penalty
The audit already confirms a compaction penalty range of 0.0 - 0.12. 


Use:

compaction_penalty = min(0.12, proof_depth_score * 0.12)
Where:

proof_depth_score = met_required_checkpoints / required_checkpoints

This prevents already-proved concepts from wrongly staying on top.

4.4 Bottleneck promotion rule
After ranking, promote a concept to bottleneck if:

bottleneck_score =
    concept_rank
  + 0.10 * blocked_downstream_count_norm
  + 0.08 * prerequisite_chain_pressure
  + 0.06 * local_error_concentration
Pick the max.

This makes bottlenecks more structurally meaningful than raw weakness.

5. False mastery detector
5.1 Audited basis
The current Topic engine explicitly detects false mastery before diagnosis. 


5.2 Proposed false mastery formula
false_mastery_score =
    0.30 * stable_profile_signal
  + 0.20 * low_transfer_penalty
  + 0.20 * low_delayed_recall_penalty
  + 0.15 * mixed_context_penalty
  + 0.15 * pressure_gap_penalty
Definitions:

stable_profile_signal

1.0 if profile mastery/readiness looks stable

else scaled by mastery state

low_transfer_penalty

1.0 - transfer_success_rate

low_delayed_recall_penalty

1.0 - delayed_recall_success_rate

mixed_context_penalty

1.0 - mixed_context_success_rate

pressure_gap_penalty

max(0, untimed_success_rate - timed_success_rate)

5.3 Flag rule
Set FALSE_MASTERY_SUSPECT if:

false_mastery_score >= 0.55, or

profile says stable/robust but both transfer and delayed recall are < 0.50

This aligns with the broader audited system where false mastery can override normal classification and bump topics upward in Coverage. 


6. Evidence spine scoring
6.1 Audited current metrics
The current engine’s evidence spine tracks:

total/recent/coach/journey points

recent/weighted accuracy

hint dependency

average response time

slow response rate

timed success

transfer success

mixed-context success

delayed-recall success

retrieval success

representation variety

recurring misconceptions 


6.2 Proposed canonical bundle
From those metrics, derive these reusable scores:

accuracy_signal            = weighted_accuracy
retrieval_signal           = retrieval_success_rate
transfer_signal            = transfer_success_rate
pressure_signal            = timed_success_rate
mixed_context_signal       = mixed_context_success_rate
delayed_recall_signal      = delayed_recall_success_rate
representation_signal      = representation_variety_score
misconception_signal       = recurring_misconception_density
hint_dependence_signal     = hint_dependency_rate
speed_signal               = 1.0 - slow_response_rate
6.3 Proposed recurring misconception density
misconception_density =
  recurring_misconception_hits / max(1, total_recent_errors)
Clamp to 0..1.

7. Hypothesis seeding
7.1 Audited base
The engine currently seeds 7 families:

PrerequisiteWeakness

Misconception

TransferWeakness

RetrievalWeakness

PressurePerformance

KnowledgeDeficit

ConfidenceEmotional 


7.2 Proposed seed rules
Each hypothesis starts with a base_seed.

PrerequisiteWeakness
seed_prereq =
    0.45 * weak_prereq_ratio
  + 0.20 * bottleneck_dependency_pressure
  + 0.20 * hint_dependence_signal
  + 0.15 * blocked_foundation_count_norm
Misconception
seed_misconception =
    0.45 * misconception_density
  + 0.20 * confusion_neighbor_presence
  + 0.20 * answer_swap_pattern_score
  + 0.15 * contradiction_error_pattern
TransferWeakness
seed_transfer =
    0.55 * (1.0 - transfer_signal)
  + 0.20 * representation_gap_score
  + 0.15 * mixed_context_penalty
  + 0.10 * stable_basic_accuracy_signal
RetrievalWeakness
seed_retrieval =
    0.50 * (1.0 - delayed_recall_signal)
  + 0.25 * (1.0 - retrieval_signal)
  + 0.15 * decay_after_success_score
  + 0.10 * latency_retrieval_penalty
PressurePerformance
seed_pressure =
    0.50 * pressure_gap_penalty
  + 0.20 * timed_failure_density
  + 0.15 * late_question_decay
  + 0.15 * stable_untimed_signal
KnowledgeDeficit
seed_knowledge =
    0.45 * low_accuracy_penalty
  + 0.20 * low_explain_signal
  + 0.20 * broad_concept_weakness
  + 0.15 * hint_dependence_signal
ConfidenceEmotional
seed_confidence =
    0.35 * confidence_tension_signal
  + 0.25 * hesitation_pattern_score
  + 0.20 * post_error_collapse_score
  + 0.20 * inconsistency_without_content_pattern
7.3 Seed threshold
Only retain seeded hypotheses if:

seed >= 0.22

Always keep at least top 2.

8. Evidence feedback on hypotheses
8.1 Audited base
The current engine already adjusts confidence using evidence spine:

hint dependency boosts prerequisite and knowledge

low transfer success boosts transfer

delayed recall failures boost retrieval

timed failures boost pressure

recurring misconceptions boost misconception 


8.2 Proposed adjustment rules
Use additive deltas before normalization.

PrerequisiteWeakness
+0.10 * hint_dependence_signal

+0.08 * weak_prereq_ratio

-0.08 if foundational prerequisite proof is already robust

Misconception
+0.14 * misconception_density

+0.08 * confusion_neighbor_presence

-0.06 if repeated contrast drills already succeeded

TransferWeakness
+0.16 * (1.0 - transfer_signal)

+0.08 * representation_gap_score

RetrievalWeakness
+0.16 * (1.0 - delayed_recall_signal)

+0.10 * (1.0 - retrieval_signal)

PressurePerformance
+0.18 * pressure_gap_penalty

+0.08 * late_question_decay

KnowledgeDeficit
+0.12 * low_accuracy_penalty

+0.08 * low_explain_signal

ConfidenceEmotional
+0.12 * confidence_tension_signal

+0.10 * post_error_collapse_score

8.3 Contradiction rules
Apply penalties where evidence clearly argues against a family.

Examples:

if timed and untimed are similarly weak, subtract 0.10 from PressurePerformance

if transfer is high but base accuracy is low, subtract 0.10 from TransferWeakness

if delayed recall is strong, subtract 0.12 from RetrievalWeakness

9. Intervention-memory feedback
9.1 Audited base
The current engine already boosts working families and penalizes stalled families. Intervention reroute is triggered when the primary family is stalled at 2+ attempts with <50% effectiveness. 


9.2 Proposed memory adjustments
For the current topic and family:

family_effectiveness = confirmed_successes / max(1, attempts)
Boost rule
If:

attempts >= 1

effectiveness >= 0.60

Then:

add +0.10 to that hypothesis

Mild penalty
If:

attempts >= 2

effectiveness < 0.50

Then:

add -0.10

Strong stall penalty
If:

attempts >= 3

effectiveness < 0.25

Then:

add -0.18

This also lines up well with Adaptation’s audited stop-list behavior around ineffective families after repeated low success. 


10. Dominant hypothesis selection
After seeding and adjustments:

normalized_confidence = softmax(adjusted_scores)
Or simpler and more interpretable:

normalized_confidence = score / sum(all_positive_scores)
10.1 Proposed dominance rules
A hypothesis becomes dominant only if:

confidence >= 0.34

and margin over runner-up >= 0.08

and evidence sufficiency gate passes

Otherwise:

no dominant

status = Defer

entry point = DiagnoseFirst

10.2 Co-cause rules
Include a co-cause if:

confidence >= 0.22

and within 0.10 of dominant

This keeps multiple plausible explanations alive.

11. Teaching mode selection
11.1 Audited base
The current engine uses 9 teaching modes in a priority cascade, then allows:

evidence override

intervention reroute if primary family is stalled (2+ attempts, <50% effectiveness) 


11.2 Proposed family-to-mode default map
PrerequisiteWeakness -> PrerequisiteRollback

Misconception -> ContrastRepair

TransferWeakness -> TransferTraining

RetrievalWeakness -> WorkedExampleFirst if comprehension weak, otherwise ConceptCompression

PressurePerformance -> ExamRescue

KnowledgeDeficit -> FoundationBuild

ConfidenceEmotional -> ConfidenceRebuild

11.3 Evidence override rules
These should fire after default family mapping.

Transfer override
If:

transfer_success_rate < 0.40

and untimed base accuracy >= 0.55

Force:

TransferTraining

This directly follows the audited example that low transfer success can force TransferTraining. 


Visual override
If:

symbolic/verbal performance poor

visual representation performance materially better by >= 0.20

Force:

VisualFirst

Worked example override
If:

explain low

independent solve very low

misconception not dominant

then use WorkedExampleFirst

Concept compression override
If:

topic is mostly learned

but retrieval/recall weak

and false mastery low

then use ConceptCompression

11.4 Intervention reroute rule
If primary family is stalled:

attempts >= 2

effectiveness < 0.50

Then:

reroute to next strongest hypothesis’s recommended mode

This is audited current behavior and should remain exact. 


12. Entry-point computation
12.1 Audited base
The current engine computes 5 entry-point types. 


12.2 Proposed decision rules
DiagnoseFirst
Use if:

evidence sufficiency < 0.35

or top two hypotheses within 0.05

or contradiction signals high

RollbackPrerequisite
Use if:

dominant = PrerequisiteWeakness

and weak_prereq_ratio >= 0.40

ContrastRepair
Use if:

dominant = Misconception

and confusion_neighbor_presence >= 0.50

ConfidenceRecovery
Use if:

dominant = ConfidenceEmotional

and confidence_tension_signal >= 0.55

ProofCheckpoint
Use if:

topic mastery state is at least Stable

and exactly 1–2 proof dimensions remain unmet

13. Proof contract algorithm
13.1 Audited base
The current engine’s 6 audited checkpoints are:

explain

independent_solve

transfer

delayed_recall

mixed_context

light_pressure

Each is computed from both profile-level averages and question-level evidence. advance_ready only when all required checkpoints are met and current level is at or above target. Evidence-based capping prevents proof level from exceeding what question data supports. 


13.2 Proposed checkpoint formula
For each dimension:

checkpoint_score =
    0.45 * profile_signal
  + 0.55 * question_evidence_signal
Reason:
the audited engine already combines both profile-level and question-level evidence; this makes question data slightly more authoritative. 


13.3 Proposed proof thresholds
Explain met if checkpoint_score >= 0.65

IndependentSolve met if >= 0.70

Transfer met if >= 0.65

DelayedRecall met if >= 0.60

MixedContext met if >= 0.65

LightPressure met if >= 0.60

JustifyMethod met if >= 0.65

DiscriminateNeighbor met if >= 0.65

RecoverAfterError met if >= 0.60

13.4 Required-by-state rules
If topic state target is Emerging
Require:

Explain

IndependentSolve

If target is Partial
Require:

Explain

IndependentSolve

Transfer

If target is Fragile -> Stable
Require:

Explain

IndependentSolve

Transfer

MixedContext

If target is Stable -> Robust
Require:

all audited six

If dominant hypothesis is Misconception
Also require:

DiscriminateNeighbor

If dominant hypothesis is PressurePerformance
Also require:

LightPressure

13.5 Advance rule
Keep the audited strict rule:

advance_ready =
  all_required_checkpoints_met
  && current_level >= target_level
And preserve evidence capping:
if question-level evidence volume is too low, final proof depth cannot exceed supported ceiling. 


13.6 Proposed evidence cap
If a proof dimension has:

fewer than 3 direct evidence items

Then:

cap that dimension confidence at 0.59

Meaning it cannot count as met yet.

14. Delayed recall obligation
14.1 Audited base
The current engine checks delayed recall obligation as part of topic analysis and writes delayed recall scheduling through timing decisions.

14.2 Proposed scheduling logic
Schedule delayed recall if all are true:

current session improved topic score by >= 0.10

proof has at least Explain and IndependentSolve met

topic still Fragile or Stable, not yet Robust

Proposed intervals
fragile gain: +2 days

stable gain: +4 days

robust verification: +7 days

Escalation
If the learner historically forgets fast:

multiply interval by 0.7

If topic is high exam leverage:

multiply interval by 0.8

15. Session blueprint composition
15.1 Audited base
The current engine generates a strategy file and computes entry points; the session blueprint layer is the natural formal extension of that. 


15.2 Proposed blueprint assembly rules
Global rules
minimum 3 steps

maximum 8 steps

maximum 2 high-load steps in a row

every blueprint must include at least one measurable evidence-producing step

every blueprint must name its expected evidence

High-load steps
Count as high-load:

independent solve

timed probe

mixed-context probe

transfer probe

Mandatory structure by mode
PrerequisiteRollback
identify missing prerequisite

quick repair or reteach

bridge back to main topic

independent solve on target topic

evidence checkpoint

ContrastRepair
side-by-side distinction

rule/feature contrast drill

classification or sort task

independent discrimination task

transfer distinction task

ConfidenceRebuild
low-friction win

guided explanation

scaffolded task

independent but light task

reflection checkpoint

FoundationBuild
concept explanation

worked example

guided practice

independent solve

transfer or retrieval

ExamRescue
baseline untimed check

timer-aware strategy coaching

light timed mini-probe

post-probe error analysis

repeat with calibrated pressure

TransferTraining
core pattern reminder

variant form exposure

mixed-context problem

transfer probe

comparison with base form

VisualFirst
visual model explanation

label-and-map task

convert visual to words/symbols

independent solve

transfer from visual to abstract form

WorkedExampleFirst
example walk-through

self-explanation prompt

partially completed task

independent task

retrieval check

ConceptCompression
compressed summary

quick retrieval cycle

compare/contrast recap

short independent check

delayed recall setup

15.3 Stop conditions
Blueprint must stop or soften if:

two consecutive severe failures

confidence collapse event

timed panic detected

misconception contamination worsens

learner exceeds fatigue threshold

16. Evidence ingestion weights
16.1 Audited base
The current ingest_coach_episode_evidence() normalizes completed coaching steps into evidence points with flags and weight calculation, halving weight if hints are used. 


16.2 Proposed base weights
explain step: 0.45

worked example completion: 0.35

guided repair: 0.40

independent solve: 0.70

transfer probe: 0.80

retrieval probe: 0.75

mixed-context solve: 0.75

timed probe: 0.80

delayed recall check: 0.85

reflection only: 0.20

16.3 Modifiers
Hint penalty
If hints used:

multiply by 0.50

This matches the audited halving rule. 


Repetition penalty
If near-identical item repeated within short window:

multiply by 0.70

High-value diagnostic bonus
If step directly disambiguates dominant vs runner-up hypothesis:

add +0.10 before clamp

Pressure-specific diagnostic bonus
If timed probe is first trustworthy pressure evidence:

add +0.08

Clamp final weight to 0.0 .. 1.0.

17. Confidence bundle
Every Topic decision should emit a structured confidence bundle.

17.1 Proposed formula
overall_confidence =
    0.30 * evidence_sufficiency
  + 0.25 * dominance_margin
  + 0.20 * historical_family_support
  + 0.15 * representation_coverage
  + 0.10 * intervention_consistency
Where:

dominance_margin

dominant_confidence - runner_up_confidence

historical_family_support

normalized effectiveness for that family on that topic

intervention_consistency

1 minus variance in outcome across recent family attempts

17.2 Output labels
>= 0.80 high confidence

0.60 - 0.79 usable confidence

0.40 - 0.59 tentative

< 0.40 defer / diagnostic posture

18. Feedback-loop closure algorithm
18.1 Audited base
The current close_topic_clinic_feedback_loop():

reruns full topic analysis

resolves intervention family

infers outcome across 6 levels

writes intervention history

schedules delayed recall if needed

reloads intervention memory 


18.2 Proposed outcome levels
Use these six:

strong_gain

moderate_gain

weak_gain

neutral

regression

collapse

18.3 Proposed outcome inference
gain_score =
    0.35 * delta_weighted_accuracy
  + 0.20 * delta_independent_solve
  + 0.15 * delta_transfer
  + 0.10 * delta_retrieval
  + 0.10 * delta_confidence_signal
  + 0.10 * delta_speed_signal
Classification:

>= 0.25 strong_gain

0.12 .. 0.24 moderate_gain

0.05 .. 0.11 weak_gain

-0.04 .. 0.04 neutral

-0.15 .. -0.05 regression

< -0.15 collapse

18.4 Intervention memory updates
strong_gain: effectiveness +0.20

moderate_gain: +0.12

weak_gain: +0.06

neutral: 0

regression: -0.10

collapse: -0.18

19. Hard invariants
These should be explicit code assertions.

The first three are direct audited principles; the rest are the natural hardening layer.

Never set advance_ready if any required proof checkpoint is unmet. 


Never reroute unless primary family is stalled at 2+ attempts and <50% effectiveness. 


Never inflate evidence weight when hints are used; halve it. 


Never emit dominant hypothesis when evidence sufficiency is below threshold.

Never mark pressure failure as knowledge deficit without untimed contrast evidence.

Never emit a session blueprint with zero evidence-producing steps.

Never schedule delayed recall without a persisted topic teaching decision.

Never allow false-mastery-flagged topics to be treated as safely advanced.

Already real in your audited engine:

18-step pipeline
