9. Misconception Rollup Engine
Module path: topic_intelligence::evidence::misconception_rollup

Role it plays:
Summarize misconception patterns from evidence and responses.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

misconception tags from evidence points

joined response facts

j_misconceptions

What it should produce:
A MisconceptionSummary:

recurring misconception labels

density

top neighbors

swap patterns

contradiction patterns

Why it exists:
The audited evidence spine explicitly tracks recurring misconceptions, and those feed the misconception hypothesis family. 


How to build it:
Count recurrence first.
Then add rolling windows.
Then add pattern grouping such as “A/B concept swap.”

Invariants:

rollup must be topic-local

misconception density must expose denominator

Failure modes:

overcounting repeated attempts on same item

treating all mistakes as misconceptions

What done looks like:
The engine can say not only that misconception exists, but which one keeps recurring.

10. Hypothesis Seeder
Module path: topic_intelligence::diagnostic_inference::hypothesis_seed

Role it plays:
Generate the first plausible causal field.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

concept states

bottleneck diagnosis

false mastery assessment

topic tensions

local graph structure

What it should produce:
Initial hypothesis rows across the audited seven families. 


Why it exists:
Diagnosis should begin with multiple explanations, not one.

How to build it:
Start with rule templates per family.
Then move to weighted seed scores.
Then add multi-cause support.

Invariants:

always seed at least top 2 plausible families

seed stage must not yet use intervention memory

Failure modes:

collapsing everything into knowledge deficit

under-seeding confidence/emotional cases

What done looks like:
Every topic begins diagnosis with a proper competing-cause ledger.

11. Hypothesis Evidence Adjuster
Module path: topic_intelligence::diagnostic_inference::evidence_adjust

Role it plays:
Use the evidence spine to update hypothesis confidence.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

hypothesis ledger

evidence spine

What it should produce:
Adjusted hypothesis scores and evidence trace notes.

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly says evidence spine feedback boosts or penalizes specific families: hint dependency boosts prerequisite/knowledge, low transfer boosts transfer, delayed recall failures boost retrieval, timed failures boost pressure, recurring misconceptions boost misconception.

How to build it:
Implement per-family positive deltas.
Then add contradiction penalties.
Then store evidence_for and evidence_against.

Invariants:

every score change must have a reason trace

evidence adjustment cannot invent new families

Failure modes:

overweighting one evidence dimension

flattening contradictory signals

What done looks like:
The engine can explain exactly how observed behavior changed causal confidence.

12. Intervention Memory Adjuster
Module path: topic_intelligence::diagnostic_inference::intervention_adjust

Role it plays:
Use prior intervention outcomes to reshape the hypothesis field.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

ic_intervention_history

current hypothesis ledger

What it should produce:
Memory-adjusted hypothesis scores plus stall markers.

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly says working families boost their own hypothesis and stalled families penalize theirs.

How to build it:
Version 1:

attempt count

confirmed success count

effectiveness rate

Version 2:

recency weighting

Version 3:

diminishing-returns markers

Invariants:

old failed families should not dominate forever

one weak attempt should not kill a good family

Failure modes:

overreacting to tiny sample sizes

ignoring strong recent changes

What done looks like:
Topic diagnosis starts to remember what has and has not worked for this learner.

13. Dominant Hypothesis Resolver
Module path: topic_intelligence::diagnostic_inference::dominant_selector

Role it plays:
Convert a hypothesis field into one working theory plus co-causes.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

seeded hypotheses

evidence-adjusted scores

memory-adjusted scores

evidence sufficiency

What it should produce:
HypothesisDecision:

dominant family

co-causes

dominance margin

confidence

defer flag

Why it exists:
The downstream teaching and proof logic need a working theory, but not false certainty.

How to build it:
Use normalized score comparison plus margin thresholds.
Add no-dominant state when evidence is insufficient.

Invariants:

no dominant family when evidence is too weak

runner-up causes should survive when close

Failure modes:

premature certainty

no room for co-causal topics

What done looks like:
The engine can commit when justified and defer when not.

14. Teaching Mode Selector
Module path: topic_intelligence::teaching_mode::mode_selector

Role it plays:
Choose the instructional posture for this topic.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

dominant hypothesis

co-causes

learner state

evidence spine

What it should produce:
One of the audited nine teaching modes.

Why it exists:
Diagnosis is not enough. The coach needs to decide how to respond.

How to build it:
Map each family to its default mode first.
Then add learner readiness compatibility checks.
Then return mode plus justification.

Invariants:

no unsafe mode for protected learners

mode must always have a dominant-reason trace

Failure modes:

rigid family-to-mode mapping

choosing high-pressure responses too early

What done looks like:
Every topic diagnosis produces a credible teaching stance.

15. Evidence Override Controller
Module path: topic_intelligence::teaching_mode::evidence_override

Role it plays:
Override the default mode when evidence strongly indicates another path.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

default mode

evidence spine

representation signals

What it should produce:
Final mode plus override reason.

Why it exists:
The audit already says evidence can override mode choice, for example low transfer forcing TransferTraining.

How to build it:
Encode only strong overrides first:

transfer override

visual advantage override

retrieval compression override

pressure rescue override

Invariants:

override must include a reason

override cannot select a mode blocked by readiness

Failure modes:

too many weak overrides

overrides fighting each other

What done looks like:
The engine can say “the default mode was X, but evidence forced Y.”

16. Intervention Reroute Controller
Module path: topic_intelligence::teaching_mode::intervention_reroute

Role it plays:
Move off a stalled family/mode and onto the next best candidate.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

current family

intervention memory

runner-up hypotheses

What it should produce:
Reroute decision and replacement mode.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this explicitly: if the primary family is stalled at 2+ attempts and under 50% effectiveness, reroute to the next hypothesis’s recommended mode.

How to build it:
Implement the audited rule exactly first.
Then add dwell/anti-thrash later.

Invariants:

no reroute before stall threshold

reroute target must come from live hypotheses, not arbitrary fallback

Failure modes:

too-fast switching

rerouting to an equally weak candidate

What done looks like:
The coach stops digging the same hole when a family clearly stalls.

17. Entry Point Resolver
Module path: topic_intelligence::teaching_mode::entry_point

Role it plays:
Decide how the session should start.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

dominant hypothesis

evidence sufficiency

tension context

proof state

What it should produce:
One of the entry-point types the audited Topic engine already computes. 


Why it exists:
Good mode, wrong opening move still fails.

How to build it:
Map:

low certainty -> diagnose first

prerequisite -> rollback

misconception -> contrast repair

confidence emotional -> confidence recovery

nearly complete proof -> proof checkpoint

Invariants:

low-sufficiency diagnosis cannot jump straight into aggressive repair

entry point must align with learner tension

Failure modes:

opening too hard

skipping diagnostic warm-up when uncertainty is high

What done looks like:
The start of the session is intentional and defensible.

18. Mastery Proof Builder
Module path: topic_intelligence::proof::proof_builder

Role it plays:
Define what “mastery” must mean for this topic right now.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

topic state

dominant hypothesis

exam context

topic type

What it should produce:
A ProofContract with required checkpoints.

Why it exists:
The audit already confirms a 6-checkpoint proof contract in the current engine.

How to build it:
Start with the audited six:

explain

independent_solve

transfer

delayed_recall

mixed_context

light_pressure

Then add conditional optional dimensions later.

Invariants:

proof requirements scale with topic maturity and diagnosis

proof contract is explicit, not implied

Failure modes:

too weak a contract for risky topics

too strict a contract for early-stage learning

What done looks like:
The engine can state exactly what must be proven before advancement.

19. Proof Evaluator
Module path: topic_intelligence::proof::proof_evaluator

Role it plays:
Score the proof contract and decide whether advancement is allowed.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

proof contract

profile-level signals

question-level evidence

What it should produce:
Checkpoint statuses, confidence, caps, advance_ready.

Why it exists:
The audit already states that required/met status is computed from both profile-level averages and question-level evidence, and advance_ready is only true when all required checkpoints are met and evidence-based capping allows it.

How to build it:
Blend profile and direct evidence.
Add evidence floors.
Add caps when direct evidence volume is too low.

Invariants:

all required checkpoints must be met for advancement

low evidence cannot fake proof depth

Failure modes:

promoting topics too early

profile averages masking weak direct evidence

What done looks like:
The engine can prove why a topic can or cannot advance.

20. Delayed Recall Planner
Module path: topic_intelligence::proof::delayed_recall

Role it plays:
Create delayed-recall obligations after significant learning.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

improvement delta

proof result

fragility

learner forgetting profile

exam leverage

What it should produce:
Delayed-recall tasks and due dates.

Why it exists:
The audited Topic engine already checks delayed recall obligation and writes scheduling signals into timing decisions.

How to build it:
Use simple fragile/stable interval bands first.
Then personalize interval length.

Invariants:

delayed recall only after meaningful learning movement

delayed recall must be attached to persisted topic teaching state

Failure modes:

over-scheduling weak gains

under-scheduling fragile gains

What done looks like:
Fresh gains reliably get checked later.

21. Session Blueprint Builder
Module path: topic_intelligence::session::blueprint_builder

Role it plays:
Turn diagnosis and mode into a concrete session plan.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

mode

entry point

proof contract

learner state

dominant hypothesis

What it should produce:
A SessionBlueprint with:

ordered steps

evidence expectations

stop conditions

fallback branch

estimated duration

Why it exists:
The topic engine should not stop at “choose mode.” It must produce a teachable sequence.

How to build it:
Start with mode templates.
Then add constraints:

max heavy-step streak

early win for fragile learners

contrast before independent solve in misconception cases

untimed baseline before pressure probe in pressure cases

Invariants:

every blueprint includes evidence-producing steps

blueprint respects learner readiness

blueprint must be finite and executable

Failure modes:

too abstract to execute

too many heavy steps

no measurable evidence outcome

What done looks like:
A coach session can run directly from the blueprint.

22. Expected Evidence Builder
Module path: topic_intelligence::session::expected_evidence

What it should produce:
Expected evidence targets like:

Why it exists:

Map step types to expected evidence outputs, then aggregate per blueprint.

Invariants:

Failure modes:

What done looks like:
The feedback loop knows what the session was supposed to prove.

23. Stop Condition Builder
Module path: topic_intelligence::session::stop_conditions

What it should produce:
Stop conditions such as:

repeated severe failure

panic under timed work

confidence collapse

fatigue threshold

misconception contamination spike

Why it exists:
Session safety should be explicit, not improvised.

How to build it:
Start with generic stop conditions, then add mode-specific ones.

Invariants:

high-pressure modes require stronger stop policies

fragile learners require earlier softening thresholds

Failure modes:

letting a bad session spiral too far

stopping too early on normal struggle

What done looks like:
The topic engine can protect the learner mid-session, not just after.

24. Clinic Feedback Loop Closer
Module path: topic_intelligence::feedback_loop::close_clinic_loop

Role it plays:
Complete the hypothesis-test-verify cycle after each clinic session.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

finished session

new evidence

prior topic decision

intervention history

What it should produce:

new topic decision

intervention outcome row

delayed recall request if needed

downstream refresh events

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly defines this closure step as a core Topic behavior. After every clinic session it reruns analysis, resolves intervention family, infers one of six outcomes, writes intervention history, schedules delayed recall if needed, and reloads intervention memory.

How to build it:
Keep it orchestration-only:

ingest evidence

rebuild evidence spine

rerun topic analysis

infer intervention outcome

write intervention history

request delayed recall if needed

emit downstream update events

Invariants:

closure always runs after a completed topic clinic session

intervention outcome is recorded before downstream refresh

Failure modes:

partial closure leaving memory stale

session evidence written but no rerun triggered

What done looks like:
A completed session always changes topic memory and future planning in a disciplined way.

25. Outcome Inference Engine
Module path: topic_intelligence::feedback_loop::outcome_inference

Role it plays:
Classify how effective the just-finished intervention was.

Belongs to main engine: Topic Intelligence

What it should read:

before/after topic signals

evidence delta

proof movement

confidence change

speed change

What it should produce:
Outcome classes such as:

strong gain

moderate gain

weak gain

neutral

regression

collapse

Why it exists:
The audited feedback loop already infers an outcome across six levels before writing intervention history. 


How to build it:
Use weighted before/after delta scoring first.
Then add family-specific success interpretation later.

Invariants:

outcome must compare against pre-session baseline

outcome must expose why it was classified that way

Failure modes:

rating low-quality evidence as big success

ignoring hidden regressions like pressure drop

What done looks like:
Intervention memory becomes reliable enough to influence future diagnosis.

How to get this Topic family built
Because the audit already shows Topic is the deepest engine and the strongest producer of downstream signals, build this family first. Coverage reads Topic outputs, Timing uses Topic-originated delayed recall and intervention follow-up, Risk reads intervention failure and topic signals, and Adaptation reads intervention history and local topic outcomes.

Build order
Topic Scope Loader

Concept State Assembler

Concept Ranker

Bottleneck Detector

False Mastery Detector

Evidence Ingestion Engine

Evidence Spine Builder

Misconception Rollup

Hypothesis Seeder

Hypothesis Evidence Adjuster

Intervention Memory Adjuster

Dominant Hypothesis Resolver

Teaching Mode Selector

Evidence Override Controller

Intervention Reroute Controller

Entry Point Resolver

Mastery Proof Builder

Proof Evaluator

Delayed Recall Planner

Session Blueprint Builder

Expected Evidence Builder

Stop Condition Builder

Outcome Inference Engine

Clinic Feedback Loop Closer

Why this order
This order follows the current audited pipeline logic:

define scope

assemble concept state

prioritize and diagnose

choose teaching response

define and score proof

execute through blueprint

ingest evidence

close loop and persist memory

What the whole Topic family should look like when finished
By the end, Topic Intelligence should behave like a real local reasoning lab:

it knows what concepts are in scope

it knows which one is the bottleneck

it knows whether the topic only looks mastered

it keeps multiple live explanations

it lets evidence and intervention history reshape those explanations

it selects a teaching posture and can override or reroute it

it defines mastery explicitly

it generates an executable session blueprint

it ingests what happened

it closes the loop by updating memory and scheduling delayed recall

That is the sub-engine depth required for Topic to truly be the brainstem of the academic coach.

The next right move is the same format for Coverage Intelligence Registry Pack, then Sequencing, Timing, Risk, and Adaptation.


proceed

I’m carrying the same build-grade registry format into Coverage next, then I’ll keep the structure consistent so the later packs for Sequencing, Timing, Risk, and Adaptation slot together cleanly.

Thought for 18s
Below is the Coverage Intelligence Registry Pack.

This pack is anchored to the audited Coverage engine you already have: 2,291 lines, an 8-step pipeline, 7 bucket classes, 4 portfolio allocation types, 8 coverage gap types, an Ebbinghaus-derived review model, complexity-aware session estimation, time-budget analysis, coverage trajectory projection, and smart caching with staleness detection. It reads Topic Intelligence signals from cached ic_topic_teaching rows and writes ic_coverage_classification plus ic_coverage_snapshots. 

 


Coverage Intelligence Registry Pack
Parent engine
Main engine: Coverage Intelligence
Parent mission: answer portfolio-level questions across subjects: are the right things being covered, what is dangerously uncovered, what is wasting time, and is there enough runway before the exam. 


Parent-owned outputs
Coverage should remain the owner of:

ic_coverage_classification

ic_coverage_snapshots 


Parent events it should consume
TopicDecisionUpdated

TopicEvidenceAppended

TopicDelayedRecallRequested

ExamProximityChanged

CurriculumUpdated

PlannerRequested

SystemRecompute

Parent events it should emit
CoverageClassificationUpdated

CoverageGapMapUpdated

CoverageBudgetChanged

CoverageProjectionChanged

CoverageNeedsPlannerRefresh

1. Topic Signal Loader
Module path: coverage_intelligence::signals::topic_signal_loader

Role it plays:
Import Topic Intelligence outputs into the coverage layer.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

ic_topic_teaching

proof contracts

evidence spines

false mastery signatures 


What it should produce:
A CoverageTopicSignal per topic:

mastery state

readiness

fragility

recall

importance

proof blocked flag

false mastery flag

delayed recall pressure

speed risk

transfer weakness

last instructional activity

Why it exists:
Coverage should not recompute topic diagnosis. The audit is explicit that Coverage begins by loading Topic Intelligence signals from cached ic_topic_teaching rows. 


How to build it:
Start as a pure adapter over ic_topic_teaching.
Then add signal normalization.
Then add staleness metadata so Coverage knows if a topic signal is old.

Invariants:

Coverage never re-derives Topic proof or evidence spine on its own

every topic signal must carry source timestamp

missing Topic rows must be explicit

Failure modes:

Coverage silently using stale Topic signals

duplicating Topic logic in Coverage

hiding proof-blocked topics because of weak adapters

What done looks like:
Coverage gets a clean per-topic signal object from Topic with no recomputation drift.

2. Bucket Classifier
Module path: coverage_intelligence::classification::bucket_classifier

Role it plays:
Assign each topic to one of the audited seven coverage buckets:

urgent_core

urgent_recoverable

high_yield_priority

mock_sensitive

exam_near_protection

fragile_maintenance

low_yield_deferrable 


Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

CoverageTopicSignal

exam proximity

urgency rank

readiness

fragility

recall

importance

Topic overrides

What it should produce:
A CoverageBucketAssignment:

topic id

bucket

base bucket

override-applied flag

bucket reason trace

Why it exists:
Coverage needs a portfolio-shaped map of the subject before it can allocate time or estimate demand.

How to build it:
Phase 1: implement base bucket rules.
Phase 2: add Topic Intelligence overrides, especially “stable on profile but unmet mastery proof gets bumped up.” 


Phase 3: add debug traces for every classification.

Invariants:

every topic gets exactly one final bucket

Topic overrides can promote but should always leave a trace

proof-blocked topics cannot stay buried in low-priority buckets

Failure modes:

good-looking averages hiding unsafe topics

over-promoting everything into urgency

inconsistent bucket boundaries

What done looks like:
Every topic lands in one clear bucket and the engine can explain the assignment in plain language.

3. Portfolio Allocator
Module path: coverage_intelligence::portfolio::portfolio_allocator

Role it plays:
Turn the bucket map into study-time allocation across the audited four portfolio types:

Rescue

Improvement

Protection

Maintenance 


Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

bucket counts

urgent ratio

average readiness

safe ratio

What it should produce:
A PortfolioAllocation:

rescue %

improvement %

protection %

maintenance %

reason trace

Why it exists:
Coverage is not just about naming urgent topics. It must decide how much of the learner’s total effort belongs to rescue versus maintenance.

How to build it:
Use the audited rules first:

Rescue if >50% urgent and avg readiness <35%

Improvement if >30% urgent or avg readiness <50%

Protection if >70% safe

Maintenance for the rest, with the documented time bands. 


Then add smoothing so allocations do not swing too hard after small topic changes.

Invariants:

percentages must sum to 100

rescue should dominate only when the underlying subject really is unstable

protection should not inflate while urgent debt remains high

Failure modes:

rescue starvation in weak subjects

too much maintenance during exam pressure

oscillating allocations between runs

What done looks like:
Coverage produces stable, explainable time shares that reflect the actual subject condition.

4. Subject Portfolio Builder
Module path: coverage_intelligence::portfolio::subject_portfolio_builder

Role it plays:
Build a full per-subject portfolio object, not just raw percentages.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

bucket assignments

allocation percentages

subject blueprint metadata

exam dates

What it should produce:
A SubjectPortfolio:

subject id

allocation plan

urgency concentration

safe-topic concentration

exam runway

dominant coverage posture

Why it exists:
The planner and UI need a subject-level package, not isolated bucket rows.

How to build it:
Wrap PortfolioAllocation with subject metadata and supporting counts.
Then add confidence fields based on data volume and freshness.

Invariants:

one portfolio per subject

portfolio must expose both allocation and underlying shape

Failure modes:

portfolio summary hiding an extremely uneven subject

no confidence indicator

What done looks like:
One object tells you how the subject should be treated overall.

5. Coverage Gap Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::coverage_gap_detector

Role it plays:
Detect the audited eight coverage gaps:

uncovered_high_yield

decaying_gains

blocked_downstream

false_mastery_suspect

proof_blocked

speed_gap

prerequisite_chain

over_invested 


Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

CoverageTopicSignal

concept graph

session histories

review history

Topic flags

What it should produce:
A CoverageGapMap:

topic id

gap type

severity

reason trace

suggested action family

Why it exists:
Coverage should name the exact form of incompleteness rather than saying only “coverage weak.”

How to build it:
One detector per gap type first.
Then merge all active gaps per topic into a severity-ranked list.

Invariants:

each gap type must be independently testable

gap detection must expose evidence, not just labels

proof_blocked must directly reflect Topic proof state

Failure modes:

vague gap detection

duplicate gaps for the same underlying issue

no distinction between “never learned” and “learned then decayed”

What done looks like:
Every coverage problem is named, severity-scored, and action-shaped.

6. Uncovered High-Yield Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::uncovered_high_yield

Role it plays:
Find important concepts or topics that have never really entered study coverage.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

subject blueprints

concept nodes

topic teaching presence

importance/exam leverage

What it should produce:
Gap rows for uncovered high-value surface area.

Why it exists:
The system must distinguish “weak but studied” from “never actually touched.”

How to build it:
Look for important topics with no meaningful Topic teaching signal or evidence presence.
Then rank them by importance and exam leverage.

Invariants:

cannot call a topic uncovered if it has real Topic evidence history

high yield must be grounded in blueprint or importance metadata

Failure modes:

counting one accidental touch as coverage

ignoring sparse but real exposure

What done looks like:
Coverage can explicitly expose blind spots, not just fragile spots.

7. Decaying Gains Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::decaying_gains

Role it plays:
Detect topics that were learned but are now leaking.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

recall

last review time

recent mastery movement

delayed recall obligations

What it should produce:
Decay gap rows with urgency.

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly names decaying_gains as a separate coverage gap. 


How to build it:
Phase 1: low recall + prior stable signal.
Phase 2: combine with overdue review model.
Phase 3: increase urgency if exam near.

Invariants:

decay requires prior meaningful learning

decay urgency must increase with exam proximity

Failure modes:

confusing never-mastered topics with decayed topics

missing recently slipping stable topics

What done looks like:
The system can say “you knew this, but it is fading.”

8. Blocked Downstream Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::blocked_downstream

Role it plays:
Find weak topics that are structurally blocking at least two downstream topics.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

concept graph

prerequisite chains

topic weakness signals

What it should produce:
Blocked-downstream gaps with blocked descendant count.

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly names weak prerequisites blocking 2+ topics as a coverage gap. 


How to build it:
Use graph traversal from weak topics.
Count weakly reachable blocked descendants.
Then rank by blockage size and exam leverage.

Invariants:

blockage must be graph-explainable

downstream count must be explicit

Failure modes:

graph cycles

overestimating blockage from weak edges

What done looks like:
Coverage knows which weak topics are dragging the rest down.

9. Proof Blocked Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::proof_blocked

Role it plays:
Expose topics that look okay but are not actually cleared because Topic proof is incomplete.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

Topic proof contracts

advance_ready

false mastery flags

What it should produce:
Proof-blocked gap rows.

Why it exists:
The audit is explicit that Topic proof can override stable-looking profile scores and bump topics up. 


How to build it:
Simple detector first:

stable-looking topic

advance_ready = false

required proof not met

Then add proof-dimension awareness later.

Invariants:

proof-blocked status must come from Topic, not rederived loosely in Coverage

Failure modes:

stable profile masking incomplete mastery

double-counting proof-blocked and false-mastery without distinction

What done looks like:
Coverage never treats incomplete proof as safe coverage.

10. Speed Gap Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::speed_gap

Role it plays:
Identify topics where accuracy is acceptable but exam-speed viability is not.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

accuracy

speed signal

exam proximity

What it should produce:
Speed-gap rows with urgency.

Why it exists:
The audit names this explicitly as a coverage gap. 


How to build it:
Define minimum acceptable speed thresholds by exam phase.
Require accuracy to be decent enough that the problem is really speed, not knowledge.

Invariants:

speed gap should not fire when accuracy itself is poor

urgency rises with exam proximity

Failure modes:

labeling knowledge deficit as speed deficit

treating all slow work as exam risk too early

What done looks like:
Coverage can identify “knows it, but too slow.”

11. Prerequisite Chain Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::prerequisite_chain

Role it plays:
Detect cases where a topic and two or more prerequisites are all weak.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

concept graph

topic weakness signals

prerequisite states

What it should produce:
Chain-gap rows with chain depth.

Why it exists:
The audit identifies this as a distinct gap from blocked downstream. 


How to build it:
Traverse prerequisites upward from a weak topic and count weak ancestors.
Flag when chain depth and weakness threshold are both met.

Invariants:

chain should be explicit, not implied

topic weakness plus 2+ weak prerequisites required

Failure modes:

false chains from soft edges

shallow chains over-flagged

What done looks like:
Coverage can distinguish one missing prerequisite from a broken foundation stack.

12. Over-Invested Detector
Module path: coverage_intelligence::gaps::over_invested

Role it plays:
Catch stable topics consuming too many recent sessions.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

recent session counts

topic stability

competing stalled topics

What it should produce:
Over-investment gap rows.

Why it exists:
The audit defines over_invested as stable topics getting 3+ sessions in 14 days. 


How to build it:
Use the audited threshold first.
Then add context later so it is harsher when urgent topics are being neglected.

Invariants:

topic must truly be stable

over-investment should be relative to broader need

Failure modes:

penalizing intentional exam polishing

ignoring neglected urgent topics while rewarding repetition

What done looks like:
Coverage can identify wasted effort, not just missing effort.

13. Review Obligation Planner
Module path: coverage_intelligence::review::review_obligation_planner

Role it plays:
Determine which topics are due or overdue for review.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

recall

last review interval

delayed recall pressure

Topic signals

What it should produce:
ReviewObligation rows:

topic id

due date

overdue flag

reason

review intensity

Why it exists:
Coverage must track review debt separately from new-learning debt.

How to build it:
Implement the audited Ebbinghaus-derived model:
optimal_interval = 1.0 * e^(recall * 3.5) capped at 30 days, overdue if interval exceeds optimal by 5+ days or recall <0.2. Topic can force reviews when delayed recall pressure is detected. 


Invariants:

review obligations must expose both optimal and actual interval

Topic delayed-recall pressure can force a review even if the formula looks okay

Failure modes:

review intervals too rigid for fragile topics

formula-only behavior ignoring Topic pressure

What done looks like:
The engine knows exactly what review is owed and why.

14. Complexity-Aware Session Estimator
Module path: coverage_intelligence::demand::session_estimator

Role it plays:
Estimate how many sessions a topic still needs.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

readiness gap

fragility

transfer gap

speed gap

recall gap

importance

Topic proof penalties

What it should produce:
A SessionDemandEstimate from 1 to 10.

Why it exists:
Coverage should measure effort, not just weakness.

How to build it:
Use the audited six-factor model:

readiness gap base 1–6

fragility +1–2

transfer +1

speed +1

recall +1

importance +1

Topic proof penalties +1–4
capped at 10. 


Invariants:

proof penalties can raise effort even when profile looks okay

estimates must be capped and explainable

Failure modes:

too-flat estimation

ignoring proof complexity

letting one factor dominate everything

What done looks like:
Coverage can explain why one topic needs 2 sessions and another 8.

15. Subject Demand Aggregator
Module path: coverage_intelligence::demand::subject_demand_aggregator

What it should produce:
SubjectDemandSummary:

Failure modes:

What done looks like:

16. Time Budget Analyzer
Module path: coverage_intelligence::budget::time_budget_analyzer

Role it plays:
Compare sessions needed to sessions available before the exam.

Belongs to main engine: Coverage Intelligence

What it should read:

historical session rate

days to exam

subject demand summary

What it should produce:
A CoverageBudget:

sessions available

sessions needed

deficit/surplus

triage flag

Why it exists:
Coverage must know when the plan is mathematically impossible without triage.

How to build it:
Use the audited formula:

available = (sessions_last_14_days / 14) * days_to_exam

needed = new_learning + review + repair

triage if deficit > 5 


Invariants:

available and needed must be shown separately

triage must have an explicit threshold

Failure modes:

hidden runway deficit

confidenceless projections presented as certainty

What done looks like:
Coverage can say whether the current pace is enough.

18. Recommendation Generator
Module path: coverage_intelligence::recommendations::recommendation_generator

How to build it:
Start with template-based actions per gap and budget state.
Then add subject-level summary recommendations.

Invariants:

recommendations must point back to evidence

recommendations should not contradict the budget state

Failure modes:

vague recommendations

recommending more work than the budget allows

What done looks like:
Coverage outputs become directly usable by Planner and UI.

Invariants:

no silent stale reads

Failure modes:

What done looks like:

1. Sequencing Signal Gatherer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::signals::signal_gatherer

Role it plays:
Assemble all sequencing-relevant signals into one clean input snapshot before any model competition begins.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

c_topic_profile

j_concept_edges

j_concept_nodes

c_learner_traits

c_academic_events

c_coaching_episodes

j_subject_blueprints

Topic and Coverage outputs

prior sequence decisions 


What it should produce:
A SequencingSignalSet containing:

weak topic ratio

fragile topic ratio

bottleneck density

foundational weakness density

confusion-heavy topic count

exam proximity pressure

confidence/demoralization indicators

average readiness spread

urgent topic concentration

time-available signal

prior model success context

sequence churn context

Why it exists:
The audit is explicit that analyze_sequencing() begins by gathering 16 sequencing signals from real data. This sub-engine formalizes that front door. 


How to build it:
Phase 1: define the signal schema.
Phase 2: compute each signal independently as a pure function.
Phase 3: attach freshness and source trace per signal.
Phase 4: add normalization rules so all models score from comparable inputs.

Invariants:

every model must score from the same signal object

signals must be normalized before comparison

missing signals must be explicit, not silently treated as zero

Failure modes:

hidden raw-table reads inside model scorers

inconsistent normalization

stale signals contaminating model choice

What done looks like:
All seven models can score from one inspectable, deterministic signal snapshot.

2. Model Scorecard Builder
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::model_scorecard

Role it plays:
Hold the scoring surface for all candidate sequence models.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:
SequencingSignalSet

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard:

model name

base score

additive bonuses

penalties

final score

reason trace

Why it exists:
The audit says each model gets a base score (0.3–0.5) plus additive bonuses before historical penalties are applied. 


How to build it:
Start with a generic scorecard struct that every model scorer writes into.
Then add ranked sorting and margin calculations.
Then add explanation strings.

Invariants:

every score must expose its base and adjustments

all model scores must be comparable on the same normalized range

Failure modes:

opaque scoring

score inflation from unbounded bonuses

What done looks like:
You can inspect one scorecard and explain why one model is ahead.

3. DependencyFirst Scorer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::dependency_first

Role it plays:
Score the DependencyFirst strategy.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

foundational weakness density

bottleneck presence

time-available signal

graph dependency depth

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard entry for DependencyFirst.

Why it exists:
The audit says DependencyFirst wins when there are foundational gaps, a bottleneck is present, and time is available; it orders by urgency rank then readiness.

How to build it:
Score up when:

foundational gaps are concentrated

prerequisite pressure is high

time budget is not yet extreme

Penalize when:

exam triage is severe

learner demoralization would make hard-first unsafe

Invariants:

should not dominate when exam is too close for deep rebuild

must care about graph reality, not just weak scores

Failure modes:

choosing deep dependency repair too late

ignoring learner morale

What done looks like:
The engine can confidently choose structural repair order when there is still runway.

4. BottleneckFirst Scorer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::bottleneck_first

Role it plays:
Score the BottleneckFirst strategy.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

bottleneck severity

blocked downstream count

fragility concentration

readiness of affected topics

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard entry for BottleneckFirst.

Why it exists:
The audit says BottleneckFirst wins when one concept is poisoning 5+ downstream topics, and orders by fragility descending then readiness ascending.

How to build it:
Boost score when:

one bottleneck dominates structural damage

many downstream topics are blocked

bottleneck repair would unlock high-yield progress

Penalize when:

the bottleneck is unresolved but learner confidence is dangerously low and easier wins are needed first

Invariants:

bottleneck must be graph-explainable

should only dominate when blockage is concentrated enough

Failure modes:

overusing bottleneck-first for diffuse weakness

repeatedly attacking one bottleneck that is not moving

What done looks like:
The model wins only when fixing one blockage is truly the best unlock move.

5. ConfidenceFirst Scorer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::confidence_first

Role it plays:
Score the ConfidenceFirst strategy.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

learner demoralization signal

weak topic ratio

fragility concentration

confidence-related topic signals

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard entry for ConfidenceFirst.

Why it exists:
The audit says ConfidenceFirst wins when the student is demoralized and more than 50% of topics are weak, and it orders easiest-first via readiness descending.

How to build it:
Boost score when:

confidence collapse or demoralization is active

there are enough medium/easier topics to generate wins

the learner needs stability before deeper repair

Penalize when:

severe exam triage makes confidence-first too expensive

foundational collapse is too extreme to postpone

Invariants:

should not be a permanent model

must not bury catastrophic bottlenecks forever

Failure modes:

comfort sequencing that avoids real repair

restoring morale but not progress

What done looks like:
The engine can deliberately bank wins without pretending easy-first solves everything.

6. ExamWeightFirst Scorer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::exam_weight_first

Role it plays:
Score the ExamWeightFirst strategy.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

exam proximity

topic importance

gap severity

time-budget stress

triage state

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard entry for ExamWeightFirst.

Why it exists:
The audit says this model wins when the exam is under 14 days away and triage is needed, and it orders by importance descending then gap descending.

How to build it:
Boost score when:

exam is near

available time is below needed time

high-yield topics still have major gaps

Penalize when:

exam is still distant enough for broader structural sequencing

Invariants:

should rise aggressively with exam pressure

must prefer yield over elegance

Failure modes:

becoming the default too early

overfitting to importance and ignoring impossible gaps

What done looks like:
The model becomes the obvious winner when triage truly matters.

7. EasiestWinFirst Scorer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::easiest_win_first

Role it plays:
Score the EasiestWinFirst strategy.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

readiness spread

fragility profile

learner morale

weak vs fragile composition

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard entry for EasiestWinFirst.

Why it exists:
The audit says EasiestWinFirst wins when confidence is low and fragile topics outnumber merely weak topics; it orders by readiness descending and fragility ascending.

How to build it:
Boost score when:

the learner needs quick momentum

there are many winnable topics

fragile topics would benefit from gentle stabilization

Penalize when:

high-value repair topics are being dangerously deferred

Invariants:

not identical to ConfidenceFirst

should favor low-friction wins, not random easy topics

Failure modes:

wasting runway on pleasant-but-low-value topics

masking systemic weakness behind easy wins

What done looks like:
The model creates momentum efficiently without turning into avoidance.

8. MisconceptionFirst Scorer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::misconception_first

Role it plays:
Score the MisconceptionFirst strategy.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

confusion-heavy topic count

fragility

misconception density

interference heat

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard entry for MisconceptionFirst.

Why it exists:
The audit says it wins when there are 2+ confusion-heavy topics with high fragility, and orders by fragility descending then urgency ascending.

How to build it:
Boost score when:

misconception-heavy topics cluster

interference is actively damaging learning

contrast/repair work should be grouped strategically

Penalize when:

confusion density is low

exam-yield triage is more important than interference cleanup

Invariants:

must coordinate with interference spacing, not fight it

Failure modes:

over-triggering on ordinary weakness

grouping misconception work in a way that increases interference

What done looks like:

9. Hybrid Scorer
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::models::hybrid

Role it plays:
Score the Hybrid strategy.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:
Full SequencingSignalSet

What it should produce:
A ModelScorecard entry for Hybrid.

Why it exists:
The audit says Hybrid wins when signals are mixed and no single model dominates; it orders by urgency ascending and fragility descending.

How to build it:
Make this the balanced fallback:

moderate bonuses across multiple mixed-signal conditions

strong penalty if a specialized model has clear dominance

Invariants:

should not suppress a clearly stronger specialist model

must remain interpretable, not “miscellaneous”

Failure modes:

becoming the lazy default

masking weak model differentiation

What done looks like:
Hybrid wins only when the learner state is genuinely mixed.

10. Historical Penalty Engine
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::history::historical_penalty

Role it plays:
Penalize models that have recently underperformed.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

ic_sequencing_decisions

recent model usage

session success outcomes

What it should produce:
Adjusted model scores and penalty traces.

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly defines the rule: if a model was used 3+ times in 14 days with under 30% session success, penalize it by 0.15.

How to build it:
Implement the audited rule exactly first.
Later add recency decay and subject-specific penalties.

Invariants:

penalty must reference actual recent outcomes

should not penalize low-sample experimentation too early

Failure modes:

over-penalizing exploratory use

ignoring that a model may have improved recently

What done looks like:
The engine stops repeating sequence strategies that have been empirically weak.

12. Topic Ordering Engine

An ordered sequence of topics.

What done looks like:

 This is important for later pivots and debugging.

14. Pivot Condition Builder
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::pivot::pivot_condition_builder

Define when the current sequence should be revisited or abandoned.

What it should produce:
A set of pivot conditions:

model-specific conditions

conditional modifiers

The audit says Sequencing defines 3 universal + 2–3 per-model + conditional pivot conditions.

worsening churn

major new exam pressure

Then add model-specific ones, such as the audited examples:

Invariants:

Failure modes:

15. Interference Pair Loader

A set of active interference pairs with severity.

16. Interference Separation Engine
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::interference::separation

Role it plays:
Push confusing topics apart so they do not sit too close together.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

proposed topic order

active interference pairs

topic priorities

What it should produce:
A separation-adjusted topic order plus constraint trace.

Why it exists:
The audit defines explicit gap rules:

confusion > 0.7 -> 4-position gap

0.5 -> 3-position gap

0.3 -> 2-position gap
and the lower-priority topic is pushed back.

How to build it:
Implement the audited gap rules exactly first.
Then add chain handling when many pairs overlap.
Then add minimal-disturbance reordering so the sequence does not reshuffle too much.

Invariants:

lower-priority topic moves, not the whole order blindly

separation must preserve as much original intent as possible

Failure modes:

over-reordering the sequence

impossible constraint sets causing loops

pushing important topics too far back

What done looks like:
Known confusion pairs no longer appear dangerously adjacent.

17. Sequence Constraint Applier
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::ordering::constraint_applier

Role it plays:
Apply interference and other ordering constraints to the proposed sequence.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

base ordered topics

separation constraints

hard/soft ordering rules

What it should produce:
Final constrained sequence.

Why it exists:
The audit distinguishes detection of interference from application of separation constraints. 


How to build it:
Build a constrained reorder pass after base ordering, not mixed into model ordering logic.

Invariants:

hard constraints must always be satisfied

soft constraints should minimize disturbance

Failure modes:

ordering logic and constraint logic tangled together

impossible constraint handling undefined

What done looks like:
The final sequence is both strategically chosen and constraint-safe.

18. Sequence Stability Monitor
Module path: sequencing_intelligence::stability::monitor

Role it plays:
Measure how much the sequence is changing over time.

Belongs to main engine: Sequencing Intelligence

What it should read:

previous sequencing decisions

current sequencing decision

per-topic positions

model changes

What it should produce:
A SequenceStabilityReport:

model churn

positional churn

top-3 changed flag

total churn

unstable flag

Why it exists:
The audit defines sequence stability monitoring as:
model_churn * 0.45 + positional_churn * 0.40 + top3_changed * 0.15, unstable if > 0.4, with a warning to consider locking a model for 3 days.

How to build it:
Implement the audited churn formula first.
Then add historical trend of churn.

Invariants:

stability report must compare against the actual last sequence

unstable flag must be formula-driven

Failure modes:

hidden sequence thrashing

overreacting to small cosmetic reorderings

What done looks like:
The system can tell when sequencing itself is becoming a problem.

19. Sequence Lock Recommender

high churn + no severe negative outcomes -> recommend lock

Invariants:

Failure modes:

What done looks like:

What the whole Sequencing family should look like when finished
By the end, Sequencing Intelligence should behave like a real order-optimization engine:

it sees the learner’s topic landscape as a structured signal field

it explicitly compares seven ordering philosophies instead of hiding one default

it learns from failed sequence models

it can choose a structural-repair order, a confidence-restoration order, an exam-triage order, or a mixed order depending on conditions

it prevents confusing topics from sitting too close together

it knows when the current order should pivot

it monitors whether sequence churn itself is becoming harmful

it persists both the reasoning and the exact per-topic positions for later planner use and self-audit

2. Phase Resolver
Module path: timing_intelligence::phase::phase_resolver

Role it plays:
Determine the learner’s current macro learning phase.

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should read:

average readiness

at-risk topic count

stable ratio

days to exam

mission state

What it should produce:
A current phase from the audited 7-phase progression:

map_and_stabilize

repair_root_weaknesses

build_mastery

integrate_and_mix

pressure_conditioning

mock_and_repair

final_readiness

Why it exists:
All later timing logic depends on phase. Reviews, retests, pacing, and mode readiness should behave differently in build_mastery than in mock_and_repair.

How to build it:
Implement deterministic entry rules first from the audited inputs: readiness, at-risk count, stable ratio, days to exam.
Then add tie-break rules when a learner sits between two phases.

Invariants:

exactly one active phase at a time

phase assignment must expose reasons

Failure modes:

phase flapping

learners stuck in early phases because thresholds are too rigid

late exam pressure ignored because readiness is still weak

What done looks like:
Any learner/subject snapshot maps clearly and explainably to one phase.

3. Phase Transition Evaluator
Module path: timing_intelligence::phase::transition_evaluator

Role it plays:
Decide whether the learner should remain in the current phase, move forward, or roll back.

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should read:

current phase

phase entry/exit conditions

phase health

risk pressure

exam target

recent progress

What it should produce:
A PhaseTransitionDecision:

stay

advance

rollback

urgent compression

reason trace

Why it exists:
Phase resolution alone is not enough. The engine must actively decide whether the current timing posture is still appropriate.

How to build it:
Start with deterministic exit rules per phase.
Then add rollback conditions driven by stall, regression, or new exam pressure.
Then add soft-transition suggestions when the learner is almost ready.

Invariants:

transitions must be based on observable thresholds

rollback must be allowed, not treated as failure

Failure modes:

phase inertia that ignores regression

premature advancement into pressure or mocks

no rollback path

What done looks like:
The engine can explain why the learner is staying, advancing, or stepping back.

4. Phase Health Monitor
Module path: timing_intelligence::phase::phase_health_monitor

What it should produce:
A PhaseHealthReport:

healthy

slipping

Why it exists:
The audit already includes phase health / stall detection with expected durations and a three-day grace period. 


How to build it:
Implement the audited expected durations first:

map = 5d

repair = 10d

build = 14d

integrate = 10d

pressure = 7d

mock = 7d

final = 3d
Then add progress-sensitive adjustments later.

Invariants:

stall logic must consider exam distance

Failure modes:

over-triggering stall for slow but valid progress

What done looks like:
The engine knows when a phase is living too long without enough movement.

5. Review Schedule Builder
Module path: timing_intelligence::review::review_schedule_builder

Role it plays:
Build the timing layer’s concrete review schedule.

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should read:

topic recall state

Coverage review obligations

Topic delayed-recall requests

learner daily capacity

exam target

What it should produce:
Timed review actions:

topic id

due date

review type

urgency

reason

Why it exists:
Coverage can say a review is owed, but Timing decides when it should actually happen.

How to build it:
Merge all review obligations into one queue.
Then prioritize by fragility, exam leverage, overdue severity, and available daily capacity.
Then persist actionable review_topic decisions.

Invariants:

every scheduled review must have a reason

Topic-forced delayed recall must not be silently dropped

Failure modes:

review overload on one day

delayed recall drowned out by ordinary review debt

no prioritization under time scarcity

What done looks like:
Reviews stop being abstract obligations and become a real calendar of actions.

6. Recall Spacing Calculator
Module path: timing_intelligence::review::recall_spacing_calculator

What it should read:

What it should produce:
A spacing recommendation:

next interval

overdue threshold

spacing confidence

Why it exists:
Review scheduling should not be flat. Topics with weak recall or high fragility need different spacing from stable topics.

How to build it:
Start with the current recall-driven spacing logic already implied by audited review scheduling.
Then add phase-aware compression near exams and expansion for stable topics.

Invariants:

weaker recall should never produce longer spacing

spacing must shorten when exam pressure rises

Failure modes:

overly rigid intervals

spacing that ignores fragility

no compression under exam pressure

What done looks like:
The engine can say not just that a review is due, but why the interval is what it is.

7. Retest Candidate Scanner

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should produce:
A candidate list tagged by retest reason.

How to build it:
Scan for three audited sources:

fragile gains

compaction checkpoints

Then emit one candidate row per reason.

Invariants:

candidate discovery should be reason-based

Failure modes:

mixing all retests into one undifferentiated queue

missing important follow-up checks

What done looks like:
The engine knows which topics need retesting and why before it schedules them.

8. Fragile Gains Retest Planner
Module path: timing_intelligence::retests::fragile_gains_planner

Role it plays:
Schedule retests for topics that recently improved but remain unstable.

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should read:

fragility

recall

transfer

speed

recent improvement deltas

What it should produce:
Fragile-gain retest actions with:

due date

retest type

objective

Why it exists:
The audit states fragile gains use a multi-dimension analysis over fragility, recall, transfer, and speed, yielding 5 distinct retest types. 


How to build it:
Start with the four audited dimensions.
Then map dimension patterns to retest types:

recall verification

transfer verification

speed verification

mixed-stability verification

pressure-safe verification

Invariants:

a fragile gain retest must name the dimension being verified

improvement alone is not enough; fragility must still matter

Failure modes:

treating every improvement as stable

scheduling generic retests with no purpose

What done looks like:
Recently improved topics get the right kind of retest, not just any retest.

9. Post-Intervention Verification Planner
Module path: timing_intelligence::retests::post_intervention_verification

Role it plays:
Schedule follow-up checks after confirmed interventions.

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should read:

ic_intervention_history

confirmed intervention rows

intervention family

outcome class

What it should produce:
Verification retests tied to intervention history.

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly names this as the second retest category: confirmed interventions need follow-up. 


How to build it:
Filter confirmed intervention rows lacking follow-up.
Then schedule a verification retest based on intervention type and confidence of gain.

Invariants:

every confirmed intervention should either have follow-up or an explicit exemption

verification must stay linked to the intervention that caused it

Failure modes:

interventions marked successful without later verification

repeated follow-ups for the same intervention

What done looks like:
The engine stops trusting intervention success too early.

Compaction/stability retest decisions.

11. Golden Window Detector
Module path: timing_intelligence::reinforcement::golden_window_detector

Role it plays:
Detect topics that improved recently and should be reinforced before the gain fades.

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should read:

recent topic improvements

reinforcement history

fragility

last touched timestamp

What it should produce:
Golden-window opportunities with expiration times.

Why it exists:
The audit explicitly defines golden window detection: topics improved in the last 48h and not yet reinforced, with a 24h window if fragile and 48h if stable.

How to build it:
Implement the audited fragile/stable window sizes first.
Then add multi-window prioritization when too many topics qualify at once.

Invariants:

a golden window requires recent improvement

a reinforced topic should not reopen the same window immediately

Failure modes:

stale gains treated as golden

fragile gains missing their short window

too many simultaneous windows with no prioritization

What done looks like:
The engine spots “reinforce now or lose leverage” moments reliably.

Why it exists:
The audit already encodes these three reinforcement types:

retrieval practice when recall < 0.4

variation test when fragility > 0.5

delayed recall by default. 


How to build it:
Implement the audited thresholds first.
Then add richer tie-breaks later for transfer-heavy topics or pressure-sensitive topics.

Invariants:

the type must be chosen from observed weakness, not arbitrary defaults

the selector must expose why it picked that type

Failure modes:

same reinforcement type for every topic

retrieval needs hidden under generic delayed recall

What done looks like:
Golden-window actions become purposeful instead of generic.

20. Timing Decision Writer
Module path: timing_intelligence::persist::decision_writer

Role it plays:
Persist every actionable timing decision into the authoritative timing store.

Belongs to main engine: Timing Intelligence

What it should read:
All upstream timing sub-engine outputs.

What it should produce:
ic_timing_decisions rows containing actions such as:

review_topic

retest_topic

phase_transition

start_timed_work

run_mock

stop_new_learning
with scheduled dates and reasons.

Why it exists:
Timing decisions must become planner-readable, UI-readable, and historically auditable.

How to build it:
Normalize every action into one canonical decision row:

action type

target topic or subject

due date

reason

originating sub-engine

confidence

Invariants:

every persisted timing action must include reasoning

write path should be idempotent for the same trigger cycle

Failure modes:

duplicate timing decisions

action rows with no reason or due date

partial persistence

What done looks like:
Timing’s full output is one clean decision ledger that other engines can trust.

Build order for the Timing family
Timing depends on stable upstream signals from Topic and Coverage, and it also reads intervention history and compaction state. The audit confirms it consumes topic/profile/events, mission state, coaching episodes, intervention history, compaction state, prior timing decisions, and subject blueprints.

Recommended build sequence
Subject Exam Target Resolver

Phase Resolver

Phase Transition Evaluator

Phase Health Monitor

Review Schedule Builder

Recall Spacing Calculator

Retest Candidate Scanner

Fragile Gains Retest Planner

Post-Intervention Verification Planner

Compaction Checkpoint Planner

Golden Window Detector

Reinforcement Type Selector

Mode Decision Engine

Daily Pacing Engine

Rest Detector

Cooldown Detector

Recommended Session Count Calculator

Session Frequency Monitor

Multi-Exam Coordinator

Timing Decision Writer

Why this order
It follows the audited timing flow:

resolve subject exam target

determine current phase

check transitions and phase health

build reviews and retests

detect golden windows

compute mode decisions

compute daily pacing and session frequency

persist all actionable timing decisions.

What the whole Timing family should look like when finished
By the end, Timing Intelligence should behave like a real temporal operating layer:

it knows which exam horizon matters for this subject

it knows what macro phase the learner is in

it knows when a phase is stalling

it knows what reviews and retests are due and why

it catches fragile gains while reinforcement windows are still open

it controls readiness for timed work, mock work, and stopping new learning

it decides how hard today should be

it detects rest and cooldown needs before burnout grows

it monitors whether the learner is over- or under-studying

it persists every timing action with reason and date

Next should be the Risk Intelligence Registry Pack.


proceed

I’m expanding the next parent engine now in the same build-grade format, keeping it anchored to the audited system so the registry stays consistent instead of drifting into generic architecture.

Thought for 17s
Below is the Risk Intelligence Registry Pack.

This pack is anchored to your audited Risk engine: 1,298 lines, a 10-step pipeline, 12 risk classes, 8 compound risk patterns, 3 early warning types, risk velocity, risk-adjusted priorities, per-class historical trend analysis, and 3-scope persistence across topic, subject, and phase rows. It reads topic/profile/graph/intervention/coverage/contrast/history data and writes ic_risk_assessments with upsert semantics. 


Risk Intelligence Registry Pack
Parent engine
Main engine: Risk Intelligence
Parent mission: protect the learner and the plan by identifying what can silently go wrong, what is already going wrong, how fast it is worsening, and what protective action should override normal planning.

ic_risk_assessments at:

topic scope

subject scope

phase scope

1. Global Signal Calculator
Module path: risk_intelligence::signals::global_signal_calculator

Role it plays:
Compute the background pressure field before any topic-level risk scoring begins.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

days to exam

subject exam target

overall intervention failure

global learner load

plan compression state

What it should produce:
A GlobalRiskSignalSet:

time pressure

exam urgency

global intervention failure rate

learner overload context

global risk multiplier hints

Why it exists:
The audited risk pipeline begins with global signals: days to exam, time pressure, and global intervention failure. Topic risk should not score in a vacuum. 


How to build it:
Start with direct calculators for:

days_to_exam

time_pressure

global_intervention_failure

Then add:

overload context

compression mode context

global confidence erosion signal

Invariants:

all topic risk scorers must use the same global context

time pressure must be explicit and inspectable

Failure modes:

topic risk ignoring looming exam pressure

no global intervention-failure context

duplicated global calculations across sub-engines

What done looks like:
Every topic risk row can explain the background pressure field it was scored under.

2. Topic Risk Feature Assembler
Module path: risk_intelligence::topic::feature_assembler

Role it plays:
Build the normalized feature set needed to score the 12 risk classes for one topic.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

c_topic_profile

j_concept_nodes

j_concept_edges

ic_topic_cases

ic_intervention_history

j_concept_coverage

ct_contrast_pairs

c_coaching_episodes 


What it should produce:
A TopicRiskFeatures object:

readiness

fragility

transfer

recall

speed

downstream blockage count

at-risk state

intervention failure rate

ARIL/content coverage

confusion score

recent improvement/regression markers

subject weak-topic density

Why it exists:
The 12 risk classes need a common feature base. Without it, each scorer becomes a raw-table interpreter and the engine gets noisy.

How to build it:
Define one canonical feature struct first.
Then compute each field independently.
Then normalize to 0..1.
Then attach source traces.

Invariants:

all risk scorers read the same normalized feature object

missing feature values must be explicit

Failure modes:

each scorer interpreting raw data differently

hidden denormalization bugs

stale intervention rates

What done looks like:
One feature row fully describes the risk-relevant state of a topic.

3. False Mastery Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::false_mastery

Role it plays:
Score the danger that a topic looks learned but is not actually safe.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

readiness

fragility

transfer

recall

false mastery flags from Topic

What it should produce:
A class score for false_mastery.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class explicitly with weight 0.12 and logic: readiness above 0.6 but fragility/transfer/recall betray it. 


How to build it:
Start with the audited logic directly.
Then incorporate Topic’s explicit false-mastery signal as a confidence booster rather than recreating it from scratch.

Invariants:

high readiness alone must not suppress this risk

false-mastery risk should rise when transfer/recall contradict readiness

Failure modes:

stable profile hiding unsafe mastery

over-scoring every fragile topic as false mastery

What done looks like:
The engine can catch “looks safe, actually dangerous.”

4. Prerequisite Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::prerequisite

Role it plays:
Score the risk from weak prerequisites that block downstream progress.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

readiness

downstream blockage count

graph dependency pressure

bottleneck markers

What it should produce:
A class score for prerequisite.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.12 and logic: weak plus blocks downstream, scaled by downstream count. 


How to build it:
Use weak-state detection first.
Then scale by blocked descendant count.
Then add exam leverage weighting to blocked descendants later.

Invariants:

prerequisite risk must be graph-explainable

downstream count must materially affect the score

Failure modes:

treating all weak topics as prerequisite risks

ignoring structural blockage

What done looks like:
The engine can tell when one weak topic is poisoning many others.

5. Retention Decay Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::retention_decay

Role it plays:
Score how likely it is that a topic is leaking out of memory.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

recall

recent review history

delayed recall pressure

stable topic markers

What it should produce:
A class score for retention_decay.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.10 and logic (1 - recall) * 0.8. 


How to build it:
Implement the audited formula first.
Then add boosts for overdue review and stable-topic decay, because decay from a previously stable topic is especially dangerous.

Invariants:

lower recall must monotonically increase risk

recently reinforced topics should not score decay too aggressively

Failure modes:

decay risk flat across all low-recall topics

not distinguishing decay from never-mastered material

What done looks like:
The engine can see memory leakage before it becomes visible collapse.

6. Confidence Collapse Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::confidence_collapse

Role it plays:
Score the danger of learner discouragement and disengagement inside a topic.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

at-risk status

fragility

tension signals

recent failure pattern

What it should produce:
A class score for confidence_collapse.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.09 and explicit tiers:

at-risk + high fragility = 0.8

at-risk = 0.5

fragile = 0.4 


How to build it:
Implement the audited tiers first.
Then add post-error collapse and repeated-failure patterns later.

Invariants:

emotional risk must not be hidden behind academic averages

confidence collapse should be separable from knowledge weakness

Failure modes:

ignoring emotional danger until motivation crashes

over-labeling every fragile topic as a confidence crisis

What done looks like:
The engine can flag when the learner is not just weak, but at risk of disengaging.

7. Overload Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::overload

Role it plays:
Score whether the learner or subject is carrying too much weak material at once.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

weak topics in subject

current load density

pacing stress

phase intensity

What it should produce:
A class score for overload.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.06 and base logic weak_in_subject / 10. 


How to build it:
Start with the audited weak-topic-density formula.
Then add pacing and daily intensity modifiers later.

Invariants:

overload is broader than one topic; it needs subject context

overload should rise as weak-topic density rises

Failure modes:

no distinction between one weak topic and a saturated subject

overload staying too low during true burnout conditions

What done looks like:
The engine can tell when the plan is asking the learner to hold too much unstable material.

8. Time-to-Exam Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::time_to_exam

Role it plays:
Score how dangerous the remaining time horizon is for a topic.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

time pressure

readiness

days to exam

subject exam target

What it should produce:
A class score for time_to_exam.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.13 and logic time_pressure * (1 - readiness). 


How to build it:
Use the audited formula exactly first.
Then add topic importance as a downstream modifier only in risk-adjusted priority, not inside the class itself.

Invariants:

low readiness under high time pressure must spike risk

low time pressure should suppress this risk even if readiness is weak

Failure modes:

same risk for distant and near exams

double-counting importance inside the class score

What done looks like:
The engine knows when time itself is becoming the threat.

9. Plan Drift Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::plan_drift

Role it plays:
Score whether the current plan is losing coherence around a topic.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

stalled topic case markers

escalated topic case markers

sequence churn near topic

repeated reroutes

What it should produce:
A class score for plan_drift.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.07 and logic: stalled or escalated topic case = 0.7. 


How to build it:
Implement the audited stalled/escalated case rule first.
Then later add neighboring-sequence turbulence and repeated reroutes.

Invariants:

plan drift must be tied to observable strategy instability

one reroute alone should not imply full drift

Failure modes:

never catching strategic incoherence

over-scoring ordinary plan revision as drift

What done looks like:
The engine can see when the plan itself is becoming unreliable.

10. Surprise Fragility Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::surprise_fragility

Role it plays:
Score topics that appear stronger than they actually are under speed or transfer stress.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

speed

transfer

recent hidden failures

stable-looking profile signals

What it should produce:
A class score for surprise_fragility.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.06 and logic (1-speed)*0.6 + (1-transfer)*0.4. 


How to build it:
Implement the audited weighted formula first.
Then add a boost when the topic otherwise looks stable, because surprise matters most when expectations are wrong.

Invariants:

weak speed and transfer must increase this risk

this class should remain distinct from false mastery

Failure modes:

collapsing surprise fragility into generic fragility

not surfacing hidden instability until too late

What done looks like:
The engine can detect “this topic is shakier than it appears.”

11. Intervention Failure Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::intervention_failure

Role it plays:
Score the danger that the coach’s current repair attempts are not working.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

topic-specific intervention failure rate

fallback global intervention failure

intervention recency

What it should produce:
A class score for intervention_failure.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.04 and says it uses topic-specific failure rate with fallback to global. 


How to build it:
Use topic-specific failure first.
If sample size is too low, fall back to global family failure.
Later add diminishing-returns modifiers.

Invariants:

topic-specific evidence outranks global fallback

low sample sizes must be handled explicitly

Failure modes:

global failure hiding local success

local failure hidden by a good global average

What done looks like:
Risk can say “the strategy for this topic is not working.”

12. Content Quality Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::content_quality

Role it plays:
Score the danger that the learner is operating with poor or thin content support.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

ARIL/content coverage

content sufficiency

topic material density

What it should produce:
A class score for content_quality.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.04 and logic (1 - ARIL coverage) * 0.7. 


How to build it:
Start with the audited ARIL-coverage formula.
Then later add content sufficiency dimensions like too few contrast tasks or too little transfer material.

Invariants:

poor content support must be visible as a risk, not hidden in performance alone

content quality should not be inferred from learner outcomes only

Failure modes:

diagnosing the learner when the real issue is content poverty

content risk always staying low because it is weakly weighted

What done looks like:
The engine can say “part of the danger is that our material support is inadequate.”

13. Interference Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::interference

Role it plays:
Score the risk that a topic is being damaged by confusion with nearby concepts.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

confusion score

fragility

active contrast pairs

recent sequencing adjacency

What it should produce:
A class score for interference.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.09 and logic confusion_score * 0.6 + fragility * 0.4. 


How to build it:
Use the audited confusion/fragility blend first.
Then add adjacency amplifiers when conflicting topics were recently studied too closely.

Invariants:

interference must be tied to identifiable pairings or neighborhoods

fragility alone should not dominate without confusion context

Failure modes:

all fragile topics looking interference-heavy

missing recent adjacency effects

What done looks like:
The engine can see when confusion, not mere weakness, is the problem.

14. Regression Risk Scorer
Module path: risk_intelligence::classes::regression

Role it plays:
Score the risk that recent gains are already slipping backward.

Belongs to main engine: Risk Intelligence

What it should read:

recently improved markers

fragility

recall

recent negative delta

What it should produce:
A class score for regression.

Why it exists:
The audit defines this class with weight 0.08 and logic: recently improved + fragile + low recall. 


How to build it:
Start with the audited triple-condition rule.
Then add gradient scaling from the size of the recent fall.

Invariants:

regression requires prior gain, not just current weakness

fragile recent gains should be riskier than old stable topics

Failure modes:

confusing long-term weakness with regression

missing fast post-gain collapse

What done looks like:
The engine can tell when progress is reversing.

15. Topic Risk Assessor

Combine all 12 class scores into a per-topic risk row.
