4. Database read/write boundaries
This is the real safety contract.

4.1 Topic may write
ic_topic_teaching

ic_topic_evidence_points

ic_intervention_history

Topic-originated rows in ic_timing_decisions

Topic may read:

mission, graph, profile, compaction, misconceptions, responses, evidence, intervention history, tensions, coaching episodes, timing decisions, prior topic teaching. 


Topic must not write:

ic_coverage_*

ic_sequencing_*

ic_risk_assessments

ic_adaptation_log

4.2 Coverage may write
ic_coverage_classification

ic_coverage_snapshots

Coverage may read:

Topic outputs, profiles, blueprints, academic events, existing coverage rows. 


Coverage must not write:

Topic tables

sequence tables

timing ledger

risk tables

adaptation tables

4.3 Sequencing may write
ic_sequencing_decisions

ic_sequencing_decision_topics

Sequencing may read:

topic/profile/graph/contrast/traits/event history and prior sequencing rows. 


4.4 Timing may write
ic_timing_decisions

Timing may read:

profile, events, concept nodes, mission, coaching episodes, intervention history, compaction state, prior timing decisions, subject blueprints. 


4.5 Risk may write
ic_risk_assessments

Risk may read:

profile, graph, academic events, topic cases, intervention history, concept coverage, contrast pairs, coaching episodes, prior risk rows, subject blueprints. 


4.6 Adaptation may write
ic_adaptation_log

ic_learner_state

Adaptation may read:

topic cases, tensions, profile, intervention history, mission state, coaching episodes, concept nodes, prior adaptation rows. 


5. Shared-fabric access policy
Not every engine should read every table directly.

5.1 Direct-read zone
An engine may directly read:

its own canonical tables

upstream canonical outputs

raw source tables it truly needs for first-principles computation

5.2 Preferred-read zone
An engine should prefer:

ic_topic_teaching instead of reconstructing topic proof/evidence

ic_coverage_snapshots instead of recomputing portfolio state

ic_sequencing_decisions instead of guessing order

ic_timing_decisions instead of recalculating schedules

ic_risk_assessments instead of re-deriving danger

ic_adaptation_log / ic_learner_state instead of rediscovering strategy memory

5.3 Forbidden-read zone
Planner should not become a raw SQL miner over all base tables once orchestration exists. It should read compiled bundles, with fallback only to engine canonical tables when necessary.

6. Invalidation rules
When one canonical truth changes, downstream snapshots must be marked stale.

6.1 Topic invalidates
If ic_topic_teaching changes materially:

invalidate Coverage if proof, false mastery, readiness, fragility, or importance-driving values changed

invalidate Sequencing if bottleneck, urgency, interference, or readiness changed materially

invalidate Timing if delayed recall, proof phase, improvement/regression, or retest-driving state changed

invalidate Risk if false mastery, regression, intervention failure, or interference changed

invalidate Adaptation if intervention outcome, stalled/regressing state, or learner-preference evidence changed

6.2 Coverage invalidates
If ic_coverage_classification or ic_coverage_snapshots change materially:

invalidate Sequencing if urgency mix or portfolio posture changed

notify Planner

optionally notify Adaptation if over-review or new-content-freeze context changes

6.3 Sequencing invalidates
If sequence model, positions, or churn changed materially:

invalidate Risk if interference adjacency or plan-drift drivers changed

notify Planner

6.4 Timing invalidates
If timing decisions change materially:

invalidate Risk if stop-new-learning, block-timed-work, or phase pressure changed

notify Planner

6.5 Risk invalidates
If overall risk, protection rules, or rising-fast state changed materially:

notify Adaptation

notify Planner immediately

6.6 Adaptation invalidates
If adaptation mode changes:

invalidate Topic if reopen_diagnosis

invalidate Timing if compress or timing_shift

invalidate Sequencing if sequence_shift

notify Planner immediately

7. Database migration order
Do not migrate the whole architecture at once.

Phase 1: canonical engine tables
Create or harden:

ic_topic_teaching

ic_topic_evidence_points

ic_intervention_history

ic_coverage_classification

ic_coverage_snapshots

ic_sequencing_decisions

ic_sequencing_decision_topics

ic_timing_decisions

ic_risk_assessments

ic_adaptation_log

This matches the current audited ownership model. 

 


Phase 2: learner-state shared fabric
Add:

ic_learner_state

This should come after Adaptation is stable enough to populate it reliably.

Phase 3: orchestration support tables
Add:

ic_engine_cycle_audit

ic_outbox_events

ic_snapshot_invalidation

Suggested schemas:

create table ic_engine_cycle_audit (
  cycle_id uuid primary key,
  trace_id uuid not null,
  trigger text not null,
  learner_id uuid not null,
  subject_id uuid,
  topic_id uuid,
  engines_run jsonb not null,
  changed_engines jsonb not null,
  conflicts_resolved jsonb not null,
  planner_summary jsonb,
  started_at timestamptz not null,
  finished_at timestamptz not null
);
create table ic_outbox_events (
  outbox_id uuid primary key,
  cycle_id uuid not null,
  emitted_by text not null,
  event_type text not null,
  payload jsonb not null,
  created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
  delivered_at timestamptz
);
create table ic_snapshot_invalidation (
  invalidation_id uuid primary key,
  learner_id uuid not null,
  subject_id uuid,
  topic_id uuid,
  snapshot_kind text not null,
  reason text not null,
  created_at timestamptz not null default now(),
  resolved_at timestamptz
);
Phase 4: optional decomposition tables
Once the family-level sub-engines are implemented deeply, add more granular tables only where needed, such as:

ic_topic_hypotheses

ic_topic_proof_contracts

ic_topic_session_blueprints

ic_coverage_gap_rows

ic_risk_compounds

ic_adaptation_stop_rules

Do not create them too early unless the current JSON/blob structures are already limiting implementation.

8. Suggested JSON vs column strategy
Use columns for:

identifiers

scope

timestamps

primary scores

primary states

booleans that drive indexing/filtering

Use JSON for:

traces

per-class score maps

proof checkpoint arrays

strategy files

recommendations

alternatives

compound pattern lists

stop lists

This is the right compromise because your current engines are rich and evolving. Lock the query-critical fields early, keep the evolving internals flexible.

9. Indexing strategy
Topic
create index idx_topic_teaching_subject on ic_topic_teaching(learner_id, subject_id);
create index idx_topic_evidence_topic_time on ic_topic_evidence_points(learner_id, topic_id, created_at desc);
create index idx_intervention_history_topic_time on ic_intervention_history(learner_id, topic_id, created_at desc);
Coverage
create index idx_coverage_classification_subject on ic_coverage_classification(learner_id, subject_id, bucket);
create index idx_coverage_snapshots_subject on ic_coverage_snapshots(learner_id, subject_id, updated_at desc);
Sequencing
create index idx_sequence_decisions_subject on ic_sequencing_decisions(learner_id, subject_id, updated_at desc);
create index idx_sequence_topics_decision on ic_sequencing_decision_topics(decision_id, position);
Timing
create index idx_timing_decisions_due on ic_timing_decisions(learner_id, subject_id, scheduled_for, action_type);
create index idx_timing_decisions_topic on ic_timing_decisions(learner_id, topic_id, action_type);
Risk
create index idx_risk_scope_subject on ic_risk_assessments(learner_id, subject_id, scope, updated_at desc);
create index idx_risk_topic on ic_risk_assessments(learner_id, topic_id, scope, updated_at desc);
Adaptation
create index idx_adaptation_log_subject on ic_adaptation_log(learner_id, subject_id, created_at desc);
create index idx_learner_state_updated on ic_learner_state(updated_at desc);
10. The final database rulebook
Rule 1
Only the owner engine writes its canonical table.

Rule 2
Downstream engines read canonical upstream outputs before considering raw-table recomputation.

Rule 3
Planner reads compiled bundles first, canonical engine outputs second, raw source tables never.

Rule 4
Every canonical row must include:

owner engine identity

updated timestamp

enough structured fields for indexable queries

enough JSON detail for explanations/debugging

Rule 5
All cross-engine recompute must be driven by invalidation, not assumption.

Rule 6
No silent dual ownership of truth.

11. What this gives you
When this schema pack is implemented:

Topic becomes the unquestioned owner of local learning truth

Coverage becomes the owner of portfolio truth

Sequencing becomes the owner of order truth

Timing becomes the owner of temporal truth

Risk becomes the owner of danger truth

Adaptation becomes the owner of strategy-change truth

Orchestration can invalidate and rehydrate state without confusion

Planner can compile one coherent next-action plan without mining half the database

That is what makes the academic coach feel like one disciplined brain instead of a loose federation of clever modules.

branch order

crate order

migration order

test order

rollout checkpoints

and what to implement first for fastest real leverage.

I’m turning this into the implementation roadmap now: what to build first, in what branch/crate order, where the leverage is highest, and how to avoid a massive rewrite that stalls progress.

Thought for 12s
Below is the Build Roadmap Pack.

This roadmap is designed around the system you already have, not a restart. The current audited stack is already real: six engines, 53 named algorithms, 12,068 lines total, with Topic Intelligence as the deepest engine at 3,996 lines; Coverage at 2,291; Sequencing at 1,675; Timing at 1,471; Risk at 1,298; and Adaptation at 1,337. It is already cross-wired: Topic feeds Coverage, Timing, Risk, and Adaptation, and the current planner already reads Risk, Adaptation, and Timing outputs to change ranking, compress plans, deprioritize reroutes, boost retests, and stop new learning. 


1. The build principle
Do not try to build the full 150k+ future brain in one pass.

The right move is to turn the existing engine into a disciplined operating system in layers:

stabilize contracts

harden data ownership

deepen Topic first

deepen the downstream engines in dependency order

add orchestration and conflict resolution

only then expand the big sub-engine families aggressively

That order fits the current audited dependency graph: Topic is already the strongest producer of local truth, Coverage consumes Topic signals, Timing/Risk/Adaptation all consume intervention history or topic truth, and Planner consumes Risk/Adaptation/Timing directly.

2. Fastest leverage first
If your goal is the biggest real improvement soonest, the first leverage points are:

2.1 Topic contract hardening
This gives you better diagnosis, proof truth, evidence quality, and intervention memory.

2.2 Planner compilation + conflict resolution
This stops engine disagreement from leaking into messy learner experiences.

2.3 Adaptation learner-state extraction
This gives you real personalization without having to fully expand every engine first.

2.4 Timing gating
This is where you stop bad pressure timing, missed reviews, and runaway new-learning drift.

Those are the moves that will make the coach feel smarter fastest, because they directly affect diagnosis quality, next-step quality, and learner safety. Topic is already the richest engine, Timing already owns phase/retest/review logic, Adaptation already owns learner-specific profile logic, and Planner already consumes those outputs.

3. Recommended branch order
I would not develop this as one long branch. Use a branch sequence that matches system dependency.

Branch 1 — engine-contracts-core
Goal:

universal engine request/response

confidence bundle

event taxonomy

engine names

shared IDs/enums

planner input bundle shell

Why first:
This gives every later branch a stable interface.

Branch 2 — db-ownership-foundation
Goal:

canonical engine tables hardened

ownership boundaries enforced

shared fabric tables added

invalidation metadata tables added

Why second:
Without clean ownership, deeper engine work will step on itself.

Branch 3 — topic-engine-hardening
Goal:

Topic registry implementation

evidence ingestion formalized

evidence spine formalized

hypothesis ledger formalized

proof contract formalized

clinic feedback loop formalized

Why third:
Topic is already the deepest engine and the main upstream source.

Branch 4 — timing-engine-hardening
Goal:

phase resolver

retest planners

golden window detector

timing action normalization

Why fourth:
Timing consumes Topic truth quickly and gives immediate learner-facing behavior improvements. The audited engine already supports phase transitions, retests, golden windows, pacing, and stop-new-learning. 


Branch 5 — risk-engine-hardening
Goal:

12 class scorers formalized

compound pattern engine

protection rules

priority builder

risk summary

Why fifth:
Risk needs stable Topic and Timing truth first.

Branch 6 — adaptation-engine-hardening
Goal:

strategy health

trigger engine

learner adaptive profile

pacing guard

stop list

adaptation log normalization

Why sixth:
Adaptation becomes much stronger once Topic, Timing, and Risk are stable. The audited engine already has triggers, learner profile, velocity, systemic patterns, dwell, and stop list logic.

Branch 7 — coverage-engine-hardening
Goal:

bucket classifier

gap detectors

review obligations

session demand

time budget

trajectory projection

Why seventh:
Coverage depends heavily on mature Topic truth. The audited engine explicitly loads cached Topic Intelligence signals first. 


Branch 8 — sequencing-engine-hardening
Goal:

signal gatherer

seven model scorers

historical penalty

interference separation

stability monitor

sequence persistence

Why eighth:
Sequencing benefits from mature Topic, Coverage, and Risk inputs.

Branch 9 — orchestrator-core
Goal:

event router

dependency scheduler

material-change gates

context hydrator

outbox

cycle audit

Why ninth:
Do this after the core engine contracts and owned tables are real enough to orchestrate reliably.

Branch 10 — planner-conflict-resolution
Goal:

hard gates

soft modifiers

conflict precedence

blocked/deferred/conditional action classes

planner rationale trace

Why tenth:
Planner should be rebuilt only after engine truth and orchestration are trustworthy.

4. Recommended crate order
Inside the repo, build in this crate order:

6. Test order
Do not test only at the end. Test by dependency layer.

shared enums

engine envelopes

planner bundle compilation contracts

Test wave 2 — Topic golden tests
Test:

evidence ingestion

evidence spine

hypothesis updates

proof gating

feedback-loop closure

This is crucial because Topic is the most algorithmically dense engine and the source of much downstream truth. The audit shows its 18-step pipeline, evidence ingestion, and feedback-loop closure are already central. 


Test wave 3 — Timing/Risk/Adaptation functional tests
Timing:

phase transitions

retest scheduling

golden windows

stop-new-learning

Risk:

12-class scoring

compound patterns

early warnings

risk priorities

Adaptation:

triggers

learner profile

pacing guard

stop list

The audit already gives you strong algorithm anchors for all three.

Test wave 4 — Coverage/Sequencing scenario tests
Coverage:

bucket assignment

gap detection

budget and projection

Sequencing:

model selection

interference spacing

churn/stability behavior

Test wave 5 — orchestration end-to-end traces
Run scenarios like:

question answered

session completed

delayed recall completed

exam proximity changed

adaptation update

system recompute

Verify:

correct engines rerun

no stale snapshots used

correct conflict precedence

correct planner output class

7. Rollout checkpoints
Use these as real gates, not vague milestones.

Checkpoint A — contracts stable
You are done when:

all engines can compile against shared domain contracts

event types are frozen enough for engine integration

planner bundle shape exists

Checkpoint B — Topic trustworthy
You are done when:

Topic evidence ingestion is canonical

Topic proof is canonical

hypothesis + intervention feedback loop is canonical

downstream engines can trust ic_topic_teaching

This is the first major leverage checkpoint.

Checkpoint C — timing/risk/adaptation operational
You are done when:

timing decisions can reliably block or schedule work

risk can issue protection rules and priorities

adaptation can produce stable strategy changes and learner-state updates

Checkpoint D — coverage/sequencing strategic layer live
You are done when:

coverage can produce stable bucket/gap/budget/projection truth

sequencing can produce stable order with interference separation and churn awareness

Checkpoint E — orchestration and planner fully integrated
You are done when:

session completion triggers the full correct recompute path

conflict resolution is visible and deterministic

planner no longer mines scattered raw tables

8. What to implement first for fastest visible impact
If you want a short list of “do these first,” this is it:

First 5 implementation wins
Topic evidence ingestion + evidence spine normalization

Topic proof contract persistence and advance_ready gating

Timing retest/golden-window scheduler normalization

Adaptation learner-state table + profile builder

Planner hard gates for stop-new-learning, block-timed-work, must-reopen-diagnosis

Why these five:

they directly improve diagnosis quality

they directly improve next-step correctness

they directly improve learner safety

they require less total engine expansion than a full rewrite

they build on logic already present in the audited engine set.

9. What not to do
Do not:

rewrite all six engines simultaneously

build orchestration before engine ownership is clear

over-decompose into dozens of tables before the parent outputs are stable

let Planner become the secret orchestrator

add deep Sequencing sophistication before Topic and Coverage are trustworthy

add very rich learner-state fields before Adaptation has enough evidence discipline

10. Suggested implementation horizon
Horizon 1 — make the current system disciplined
Goal:

contracts

ownership

Topic hardening

planner hard gates

This gives immediate quality improvement.

Horizon 2 — make the system safe and adaptive
Goal:

Timing hardening

Risk hardening

Adaptation hardening

learner-state fabric

This makes the coach smarter and less dangerous.

Horizon 3 — make the system strategic
Goal:

Coverage hardening

Sequencing hardening

full planner compilation

orchestration cycle audits

This makes the coach feel like one system instead of several modules.

Horizon 4 — expand toward the full intelligence lattice
Goal:

deeper sub-engine decomposition

more granular tables

richer experimentation

stronger meta-evaluation

broader content intelligence

11. Bottom line
The right path is not “build everything now.” It is:

stabilize the skeleton you already have

deepen Topic first because it is the main truth source

harden Timing/Risk/Adaptation next because they most directly affect learner experience and planner behavior

then bring Coverage and Sequencing into a more disciplined strategic layer

then finish the system with orchestration, conflict resolution, and richer decomposition

That path respects the actual audited system you already own instead of fighting it. Topic is already the heaviest reasoning engine, Coverage already depends on cached Topic signals, Risk/Adaptation/Timing already feed planner decisions, and the current planner already enforces meaningful downstream behavior from those engines.

The strongest next move is a Phase 1 execution pack: exact file paths, first branch tasks, first migrations, first tests, and first acceptance criteria for the first 2–3 weeks.

Branch C — topic-engine-hardening
Purpose:
make Topic the first trustworthy canonical truth source.

The audit already shows Topic is the densest engine: 18-step pipeline, 7 hypothesis families, 9 teaching modes, 6-checkpoint mastery proof contract, 17-metric evidence spine, and clinic feedback-loop closure. Coverage also explicitly reads cached Topic signals. 

 


Files to add
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/lib.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/engine.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/context.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/contracts.rs

/crates/topic-intelligence/src/evidence/evidence_ingest.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/evidence/evidence_spine.rs

/crates/topic-intelligence/src/diagnostic_inference/evidence_adjust.rs

/crates/topic-intelligence/src/diagnostic_inference/dominant_selector.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/proof/proof_builder.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/proof/proof_evaluator.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/feedback_loop/close_clinic_loop.rs

/crates/topic-intelligence/src/repo/read.rs
/crates/topic-intelligence/src/repo/write.rs
What must be implemented in Phase 1
1. Evidence ingestion
Deliver:

canonical EvidencePoint

step-type to evidence-point mapping

hint penalty

timed/transfer/mixed/delayed/retrieval flags

This already exists conceptually in the current engine and should be formalized first. 


2. Evidence spine
Deliver:

weighted accuracy

recent accuracy

hint dependency

timed success

transfer success

delayed recall success

mixed-context success

retrieval success

representation variety

recurring misconception density

These are already part of the audited Topic evidence spine. 


3. Hypothesis ledger
Deliver:

seed 7 families

evidence adjustments

intervention-memory adjustments

dominant + co-causes

defer/no-dominant state

The 7 families and 3-layer hypothesis behavior already exist in the audited Topic engine. 


4. Proof contract
Deliver:

canonical checkpoint model

required dimensions

advance_ready

evidence cap

The current engine already has a 6-checkpoint proof contract and strict advancement gating. 


5. Clinic feedback loop
Deliver:

ingest session evidence

recompute Topic decision

infer intervention outcome

write ic_intervention_history

request delayed recall if needed

This is the audited hypothesis-test-verify loop and should be preserved. 


Acceptance criteria
a completed topic session produces new evidence rows

Topic recompute updates ic_topic_teaching

proof contract is persisted and advance_ready is computed canonically

intervention outcome is written canonically

delayed recall request can be emitted from Topic

Branch D — timing-actions-normalization
Purpose:
normalize the learner-facing “what happens next” timing ledger.

Timing already owns review, retest, phase transition, start-timed-work, run-mock, and stop-new-learning decisions. 


Files to add

/crates/timing-intelligence/src/persist/decision_writer.rs
What must be implemented in Phase 1
1. Phase resolver
Just enough to support:

current phase

phase transition

start-timed-work eligibility

run-mock eligibility

2. Retest normalization
At minimum:

post-intervention verification retest

delayed recall follow-up

fragile-gain retest candidate detection

3. Golden window detector
At minimum:

detect recent improvement with no reinforcement yet

emit reinforcement timing action

4. Timing action writer
Everything must land in canonical ic_timing_decisions.

Acceptance criteria
Topic delayed recall request can become a persisted timing action

a confirmed intervention can produce a retest timing action

phase state can drive start_timed_work and run_mock

stop_new_learning can exist as a first-class timing decision

2. Family effectiveness
Need:

per-family attempts

recent success

historical success

3. Learner profile v1
Need:

preferred families

avoided families

avg successful session length

pressure response

confidence scaffolding need

These are already part of the audited learner adaptive profile. 


4. Persist to ic_learner_state
This is the first shared fabric table that other engines can read later.

Acceptance criteria
learner profile row exists and updates after enough intervention data

family effectiveness report can be generated

planner-ready adaptation row can still be written to ic_adaptation_log

low-sample profile fields remain explicitly tentative

Branch F — planner-hard-gates
Purpose:
make the planner safe before making it sophisticated.

The current planner already reads risk, adaptation, and timing outputs and applies boosts, penalties, retest priority, compress behavior, and stop-new-learning behavior. 


Files to add

Hard gates to implement first
StopNewLearning

BlockTimedWork

MustReopenDiagnosis

RestRequired

CooldownRequired

Soft modifiers to implement first
risk boost

protection boost

adaptation protect boost

adaptation reroute penalty

retest boost

compress reduction

These map closely to what the current planner already does. 


Acceptance criteria
planner can block actions, not just rank them

planner can output Blocked, Deferred, and Conditional action states

retest-due-today can outrank ordinary study tasks

stop_new_learning prevents new-topic actions from appearing in DoNow

Phase 1 success criteria
Phase 1 is successful when all of these are true:

1. Topic is a trustworthy local truth source
Meaning:

evidence is canonical

proof is canonical

intervention memory is canonical

delayed recall requests are canonical

2. Timing decisions are canonical actions
Meaning:

no loose scheduling logic scattered elsewhere

all major timing actions land in ic_timing_decisions

3. Learner-state fabric exists
Meaning:

Adaptation can persist first real learner-specific fields in ic_learner_state

4. Planner obeys hard safety/readiness gates
Meaning:

it can truly block or defer, not just reprioritize

5. Engine ownership is clean
Meaning:

each engine writes only its canonical tables

downstream consumers read upstream truth instead of recreating it

What to postpone until Phase 2
Do not force these into Phase 1:

full Coverage gap family

full Sequencing model family

full Risk 12-class hardening

full Adaptation trigger ecosystem

full orchestrator cycle manager

full conflict-resolution engine

deep JSON decomposition into many child tables

Those are valuable, but they are not the best first leverage.

The real Phase 1 hot path
If you implement nothing else, make sure this one path works cleanly:

SessionCompleted → Topic recompute → Timing action generation → Adaptation learner-state update → Planner hard-gated next actions

That is the shortest route to a coach that feels meaningfully smarter and safer.

The next strongest step is a Day-by-day sprint board for Week 1, with exact tickets under each file path and estimated dependencies.
